Discussion Title: Should the US adopt stricter gun controls?

1. The US should adopt stricter gun control legislation, in the form of the policy defined in the discussion info \(click top left menu =\> Info\).
1.1. Con: This policy would do significant harm to weapons manufacturers and sellers.
1.1.1. Con: Industry needs change, and with them employment needs. Think of coal, newspapers, or landline phones. Technological and societal changes have more or less killed these industries.
1.1.1.1. Pro: The thesis statement makes no timeline claim so presumably the market could be given time to react. There are many good gun uses that may be collateral damage of gun regulations, presumably new markets may open up to meet that demand.
1.1.1.2. Pro: Gun manufacturers can retool to produce other high-demand equipment - and given the money that was being spent on personal firearms will still be in the economy, they'll have customers with available disposable income to target.
1.1.2. Con: The loss of life as a result of gun violence outweighs short term job loss as the market adjusts to decreased demand for guns.
1.1.2.1. Con: However the loss of life and increase in violent crime resulting from an unarmed public outweighs the loss of life from gun violence.
1.1.2.1.1. Con: That's assuming more guns result in less violence, which is the premise both sides are most likely to disagree on. This very premise is often the core of the debate, it's a pro-gun only premise.
1.1.3. Con: Gun culture will not disappear overnight. If high rate of fire/capacity guns become taboo, then other models will take priority.
1.1.3.1. Con: By virtue of the proposed policy, these would also be banned.
1.1.4. Pro: Regulations could favor larger weapons manufacturers and distributors over local businesses.
1.1.4.1. Con: Many gun owners support both American-made guns and small businesses. They are not likely to turn to larger companies. In fact they would probably flock to those businesses more after the regulation to make sure they don't go out of business.
1.1.4.1.1. Con: Except they are not always able to do so. California drove [literally every single gun shop](http://www.npr.org/2015/10/27/451202615/san-franciscos-last-gun-shop-calls-it-quits) out of business in San Francisco due to excessive regulations, with no indication that additional laws would not be passed until gun store owners decided to give up, the last one deciding to close it's doors under the threat of even more restrictions.
1.1.4.2. Pro: Larger companies are held more accountable and have more eyes on them than smaller businesses.
1.1.5. Con: Legislation being damaging to the economy shouldn't be a barrier to legislation. It should be assessed and minimised where possible. But the driving force behind legislative change should be health and welfare, morals and ethics, public safety, driving society forwards.
1.1.6. Con: Weapons manufacturers would be free to leverage their capital and production experience towards more socially constructive industries.
1.1.7. Con: This is also an argument for legalising drug sales, and nuclear weapon sales. No product's legal status \(eg free/restricted/banned\) could ever be changed if deleterious effects on manufacturers could not be tolerated. It also follows that companies that are already suffering harm due to legal restrictions should be afforded relief.
1.1.7.1. Con: It is not an argument for "legalising nuclear weapon sales." That is absurd. The product's legal status is protected in the supreme law of the country as an inalienable individual right which cannot be infringed by government. Nuclear weapons are not "common", which is the standard for "arms". Companies that have sold hundreds of millions of common firearms to citizens for legitimate defensive and other purposes are not to blame for the extremely small fraction of guns that are misused.
1.1.7.1.1. Con: Illegal drugs are common across the US. There are many drug users that do not cause harm to themselves and others, and many drug manufacturers and sellers that make profit and support families.
1.1.8. Con: By implementing the proposed bill in this discussion, the US could energize an industry of non-lethal weapons used in lieu of lethal alternatives to home invasions and personal defense. Consider the market for things like [tasers](https://www.srselfdefense.com/blog/handgun-vs-taser-gun-which-one-is-better-for-self-defense/) and [salt guns](https://futurism.com/salt-the-gun-that-doesnt-shoot-bullets/).
1.1.9. Con: Not necessarily \(see: [Australian gun ownership rises](https://www.smh.com.au/national/record-gun-sales-bring-australias-firearm-arsenal-to-highest-level-since-the-port-arthur-massacre-20160427-goftbj.html)\), as with any business they would pivot into selling the kinds of guns which would be legally accessible. Semi- and fully- automatic sales would drop, but other types would rise. [Gun owners are not going to stop buying guns](http://www.abc.net.au/news/2016-04-28/australia-has-more-guns-than-before-port-arthur-massacre/7366360) just because new policies are in place.
1.1.10. Pro: Decreasing the demand for guns could lead to massive lay offs in the gun sector which [employs](https://www.nssf.org/government-relations/impact/) a significant number of Americans.
1.1.10.1. Con: That's 0.1% of the population or 300,000 jobs. That's not significant in any means, especially when those manufacturers and employees could pivot to a different market.
1.1.10.2. Con: -> See 1.1.2.
1.1.10.3. Con: This data appears to include all jobs at supplier companies for gun manufacturers, many of whom are unlikely to solely be supplying - or only be capable of supplying - gun manufacturers.
1.1.10.4. Con: This report does not show the working for their employment figures, but given they've not explicitly excluded them, it seems likely that they've included jobs related to the production and sale of weapons and ammunition to the military - a major purchaser, and one unaffected by this policy.
1.1.10.4.1. Pro: Law enforcement and military purchases account for [40% of revenue](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/wonk/wp/2012/12/19/seven-facts-about-the-u-s-gun-industry/?utm_term=.377cc0cf6a8c) for domestic arms manufacturers in the USA.
1.1.10.5. Con: The increase in gun control and enforcement would create new sectors and demand for labor including background checking and licensing.
1.1.10.6. Con: Local manufacturers could still export their guns to foreign countries. Stricter gun laws in the US do not affect the demand for guns abroad.
1.1.10.6.1. Con: It seems improbable that this number would get anywhere near to compensating the loss of domestic demand given how many guns currently exist in the US.
1.1.10.6.2. Con: Many countries look to the US as a model for government and take cues on policy from America. Instituting wide range gun reform is likely to lead to similar policy abroad.
1.1.10.6.3. Pro: Overseas gun sales already account for [over 1/3](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/wonk/wp/2012/12/19/seven-facts-about-the-u-s-gun-industry/?utm_term=.377cc0cf6a8c) of the total revenue for American arms manufacturers.
1.1.10.6.4. Pro: The Trump administration is rolling back regulations and red tape to make it easier for gun manufacturers to compete [overseas](http://www.newsweek.com/trumps-administration-looking-make-it-easier-sell-us-guns-overseas-667905).
1.2. Pro: Stricter regulation would make people consider their decision to own a gun more seriously.
1.2.1. Pro: 3% of the U.S. population owns half the civilian guns in the U.S. [qz.com](https://qz.com/1095899/gun-ownership-in-america-in-three-charts/) Though a cap on total number owned per capita is not mentioned, presumably there would be a drastic reduction of number of guns owned by this 3%, which would help reduce the total number of guns in circulation.
1.2.1.1. Con: Do note these people might see their guns as museum pieces, especially if they are rare \(e.g: World War II rifles, and going further back in time, up to black powder rifles\). I expect [this guy](https://www.youtube.com/user/ForgottenWeapons/featured) to be one of said 3% for example, and I'm pretty OK with that.
1.2.1.1.1. Con: Someone collecting non-functional museum pieces is likely to be able to get some form of specialised license, or to partner their collection with an actual museum.
1.2.1.1.1.1. Con: Would you require collectors of anything else to partner with a museum?
1.2.1.1.2. Pro: Often these museum pieces are incapable of firing or inadvisable to fire.
1.2.1.2. Con: That argument does not support the claim above it. If only 3% of people own the majority of arms in the US, that cohort is very unlikely to “think twice,” about buying more guns, or giving up any already owned.
1.2.1.2.1. Pro: If the stated goal of wanting stricter regulations was to make people consider purchases more carefully, but the reason is the hope current gun owners will purchase less guns, then the true goal would not be regulations for the sake of careful consumer consideration but rather to create future hurdles/hardship for those who have already decided that they want to purchase/own guns.
1.2.1.3. Con: Statistic is debatable BUT it is not unreasonable that a very small percentage of Americans own the majority of guns. Most gun owners own more than 1. Different guns suit different purposes. If you hunt more than 1 type of game, you own more than 1 gun. If your children hunt with you, you own their guns, too. If you carry for self defense, it's usually a handgun and many people have more than 1 for different CC situations. At home, shotguns and AR are generally more effective than handguns.
1.2.1.4. Con: 3% of people holding lots of guns isn't a problem, because you can only use 1-2 guns at time. One person who owns many guns is not inherently more dangerous than a person with one.
1.2.1.5. Con: There is no evidence to suggest that this 3% is the source of weapons used in crime or that total number of guns in circulation has a direct correlation to crime.
1.2.1.6. Con: While it may reduce the amount of guns by 3%, it will not reduce the important 3% of violent criminally inclined people.... the people who respect the law would turn in guns and those who don't will continue to break the law.
1.2.1.7. Con: Many people different or multiple own guns for specific reasons, a .22lr will not kill an elk but a .45-70 would be too much gun for a squirrel or rabbit if you plan to eat the animal.
1.2.2. Con: Instead of criminalizing gun ownership, we should be encouraging responsible people to buy guns in order to protect their own lives and the lives of others who choose not to purchase a firearm.
1.2.2.1. Con: This is a fair ideal but it raises the issue as to what people would be defending against. Other guns? The problem ends up looping infinitely.
1.2.2.2. Con: This presumes that people who purchase guns and later use them in crime have done so with crime as their intent for purchase.
1.2.2.3. Con: An individual bringing a gun to any kind of conflictual situation is not a good idea. If an armed criminal wants to kill someone chances are, whether or not the victim has a gun, is not going to change the outcome of the encounter. If a thief points a weapon at you that should be your insurance's concern. If some drunk guy wants to brawl chances are bringing a gun to this will only worsen the situation.
1.2.3. Con: Regardless of what firearm you purchase, current regulation of background checks \(initial and for every purchase\), license courses, and fees already make people think long and hard about the decision, as the government then lists all purchases and keeps purchasing histories.
1.2.3.1. Con: The government does not list all purchases, and [no complete firearm database is yet implemented](https://www.concealedcarry.com/law/are-guns-registered/).
1.2.4. Con: This logic hasn't applied to drugs or alcohol. People still drink & do drugs regardless of the law.
1.2.4.1. Con: Trying to buy illegal drugs is a painfull process that might end up with the buyer being just robbed of his money without having the product in exchange or sold bad quality products or having troubles with criminals. People still do it but with more difficulty if they don't already know reliable dealers and less often than if it was accessible in local supermarket's
1.2.4.2. Con: The implication wasn't for prohibition, but for regulation influencing behavior. Regulations around drinking and driving, for example, has had a significant impact on that set of behaviors.
1.2.4.3. Pro: The comparison with drug laws and gun control laws should be applied in pro-gun law discussions rather than as a con. Drug laws were introduced to have the intended effect of making it harder to obtain drugs. If applied to guns, this would also benefit the number of mass shootings America experiences. It is an Americans choice to buy a gun, just as it is a choice to buy drugs. Put simply, gun control laws will make it harder to obtain, which means that it is not as easy to cause a mass shooting.
1.2.5. Con: Gun control would only remove guns from law-abiding citizens. Criminals would still have their guns as they do not follow the laws therefore they would not surrender their guns.
1.2.5.1. Con: Murder is 100% illegal, but that still happens. Banning bad things allows us to punish people when they do the bad thing.
1.2.5.1.1. Con: Guns are not inherently immoral, weakening their inclusion on a list of "bad things."
1.2.5.1.1.1. Con: At least in the context of relating to humans, guns were designed with the sole purpose of ending life.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1. Pro: Killing people is a generally immoral concept.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1. Con: Not every act of killing another human being is immoral. Especially in cases of self defense, or defense of another.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1. Con: The right to self-defense is a proportional right, and having a gun makes it more likely that someone will respond disproportionally, i.e. a lethal response to a non-lethal threat.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.1. Con: There are situations in which a gun is the proportionate response.  It is the responsibility of the gun owner to understand the legal and moral ramifications of using a gun in self-defense. Rather, that is an argument for gun owners being properly educated and trained.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.2. Con: This proportion is not linear. An individual actively threatened with serious bodily harm should not be required to anticipate the ultimate extent of the assailant's intent and be accordingly meticulous with the measure of force returned. The assailant has forfeited this protection in threatening serious harm.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3. Con: That would always be left for a court to decide.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1. Con: It is better to attempt to stop shootings in the first place, rather than depending solely on post-facto punishment as a deterrent.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.1. Pro: "Stand your ground" laws and self-defense can be abused by bad-faith attackers, since, in many cases, the other party is not around to give their side of the altercation.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.1.1. Con: While any law or right can be abused, it is better to allow people the right to self-defense because it is good for innocent people to defend themselves, rather than to revoke that right because it might be abused. It is better to err on the side of the innocent.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.1.1.1. Con: Self defence does not require a gun or firearm, as many other countries in the world prove quite adequately.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.1.2. Pro: "Stand your ground" laws empower people to use violence, making shootings more likely.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.1.2.1. Pro: There is [evidence](https://www.vox.com/policy-and-politics/2018/3/2/17050610/guns-shootings-studies-rand-charts-maps) that Stand Your Ground laws increase violent crime.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.1.2.1.1. Con: According to your link, "That’s not enough for nonpartisan researchers at RAND to make sweeping conclusions ..."
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.1.2.1.2. Pro: Authorities in Florida are refusing to charge a man for shooting another man for pushing him, under [Stand Your Ground](https://www.nationalreview.com/2018/07/mcglockton-shooting-gun-owners-outraged/) laws.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.1.2.2. Con: Just because shootings may be more likely under Stand Your Ground Laws, that does not mean that those shootings will be more likely to be unjustifiable or in bad faith.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.2. Con: Removing firearms as a variable would not prevent altercations. from becoming lethal.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.2.1. Con: The claim “where persons have a motive to kill one another, they will” is flawed because it is easier to simply pull a trigger on a gun than it is to stab or beat someone to death.  The physical action is easier, meaning you couldn’t kill as many people by hand as you could in a mass shooting.  But also the experience of killing someone by hand, potentially having to grapple with them and experience their pleas or suffering, is more stressful on the assailant than pulling a trigger at distance.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.2.1.1. Con: This ignores pressure cooker bombs, pipe bombs, Timothy McVeigh and people who fly planes into buildings.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.3. Pro: The feeling of power that a gun gives may actually lead to people being [more willing](http://not everyone with a gun or other weapon will be a rational or sensible actor who is afraid of the costs of a fight with guns or otherwise, so the deterrent of equivalent force may not always result in deescalation.") to escalate a situation, equivalent force or not, because they feel overconfident about their ability to win a conflict.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.4. Pro: The use of a gun in justifiable self-defense is the most direct way to stop a an innocent person from being shot.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.5. Pro: Stopping crimes before they occur means fewer people getting shot.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.6. Con: Post-facto deterrence, even with lethal force by police officers, will not deter people from committing gun crimes who are either suicidal or insane.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.7. Con: Gun control would not stop a shooting if someone already had access to a gun through illegal means.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.8. Con: It may be better to prevent a shooting, but prevention may require extreme powers afforded to law enforcement that would cost too much in terms of money, freedom, and manpower.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.4. Con: The rampant misuse of lethal force in self-defense is tempered by the fear of being charged with manslaughter, murder, or other crimes after the incident occurs.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.5. Con: The likelihood of lethal force being used has more to do with the individual decision to use force rather than the tools at their disposal. The choice and nature of the individual precedes the operation of their tools.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.5.1. Con: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.3.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.5.2. Con: Possessing a fire arm actually increases the likelihood that you get shot.   [www.newscientist.com](https://www.newscientist.com/article/dn17922-carrying-a-gun-increases-risk-of-getting-shot-and-killed/)
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.5.2.1. Con: This study did not study cause and effect, armed people could be getting shot more often because they live in dangerous neighborhoods and therefore are more likely to be shot regardless of whether they are armed or not.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.5.2.1.1. Con: Gun owners who say they live in unsafe neighborhoods are [not more likely](http://www.pewsocialtrends.org/2017/06/22/the-demographics-of-gun-ownership/) to say the reason they own a gun is for protection.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.5.2.1.1.1. Con: I did not say they owned guns because they lived in unsafe neighborhoods but that they could be getting shot more often because they live in unsafe neighborhoods.  According to your link[Two-thirds of gun owners cite protection as a major reason for owning a gun](http://www.pewsocialtrends.org/2017/06/22/the-demographics-of-gun-ownership/)
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.5.2.1.2. Con: Urban areas have significantly [lower numbers](http://www.nytimes.com/2013/03/10/us/rate-of-gun-ownership-is-down-survey-shows.html?pagewanted=all&mtrref=www.theatlantic.com&gwh=EB3C06B7AEC5DCD727CEE14A560B532C&gwt=pay) of firearms than rural areas.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.5.2.1.2.1. Con: Your article does not compare urban to rural areas, it compares mountain and southern regions \(which include the Dallas Fort Worth area, Houston, Austin, El Paso. Denver, etc. to the North East.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.6. Con: Any weapon can be used as a disproportionate response to a non-lethal threat, including one's own hands.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.6.1. Con: Most means of killing with common, non-firearm weapons are likely to take longer and can be stopped by a defender before being lethal. \(Strangulation: people can be revived if treated quickly and the defender can stop when the attacker passes out. Brawling: typically ends with one fighter being knocked unconscious; again the defender can stop before beating the attacker to death. Short knife: a single knife wound can be enough to stop an attacker without being lethal.\)
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.7. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.3.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.8. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.5.2.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9. Pro: The misapplication of lethal force in a self-defense situation is a downside to allowing people to own guns for self defense.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1. Pro: It is hard to scale use of a gun proportionately to non-lethal threats.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.1. Con: It may be hard, but the onus is on the gun user - it's against the law to use a gun disproportionately.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.1.1. Con: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.2. Con: The only legal use of a gun is in defensive response to a lethal threat. Therefore, in fact the difficulty is not in scale, but in the fast and accurate shooting of the gun to neutralize the threat.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.2.1. Con: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.2.2. Con: Hunting for food is a legal use of firearms.  Killing predators that threaten livestock or pets is also a legal use of firearms.  Shooting skunks, wild hogs, and other pests is also legal.  If you need to kill your animals because it is disabled or so sick that it will not recover and suffering is also legal if firing a weapon is legal where you live \(typically rural areas\).
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.3. Pro: There is only one setting on a gun, you cannot shoot someone "less hard."
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4. Con: It is easy to scale use of a gun proportionally to non-lethal threats.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.1. Pro: You can tell the aggressor that you have a gun.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.1.1. Con: This is not a good idea unless the aggressor is on your porch and breaking down your door and you are in your house.  By announcing that you have a gun, you could be charged with disorderly conduct, making threats with a firearm, etc.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.2. Pro: You can show the aggressor your holstered gun.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.2.1. Con: This could be considered a threat where the "aggressor" claims self defense because they perceive that you are threatening to shoot them.  If they are armed, or fast and close enough they could prevent you from using your holstered gun.  If you are only authorized for concealed carry, this could be considered a breach of concealment and therefore breaking the law.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.3. Pro: You can put you hand on your holstered gun.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.3.1. Pro: This is good, only if you are preparing to actually draw your weapon from the holster.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.4. Pro: You can unholster your gun, pointing it away from the aggressor.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.4.1. Con: If you draw your firearm you need to be ready to use it. If you point it away from the aggressor unless you are pointing it down but only need to raise it to aim at the aggressor, you are less prepared to use it.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.5. Pro: You can chamber a round in your gun / cock the gun.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.5.1. Con: If you have not chambered a round, your gun is not ready to use.  This could lead to you having no opportunity to use your weapon because you are trying to chamber a round while being rushed by an attacker.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.6. Pro: You can fire your gun away from the aggressor to prove that it is functional.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.6.1. Con: This puts innocent bystanders potentially in danger.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.6.2. Con: This seems like an incredibly effective method of provoking someone into attacking you or shooting you in what would then, presumably, become self-defense.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.6.3. Con: This only proves that you have one round in the firearm.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.7. Pro: You can aim the gun at the aggressor without firing.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.7.1. Con: This is only viable if you are prepared to actually fire if necessary.  If you are just blustering, you are more likely to get yourself killed because you are not actually prepare to defend yourself.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.8. Pro: You can fire in the general direction of the aggressor without intention to hit him.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.8.1. Con: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.6.1.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.8.2. Con: There is so much wrong with this suggestion.  It is just reckless.  How well will you be aiming in a general direction?  Unless you know where you are very well you do not know what may be behind the aggressor.  A miss can be devastating unless you are at a shooting range which has an appropriate barrier behind the targets.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.9. Pro: You can fire your gun at the aggressor in less-lethal areas of the body \(arms/legs\).
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.9.1. Con: Most people are incapable of aiming a gun precisely enough to "wound" rather than "kill" in a stressful situation.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.9.1.1. Pro: The margin of error for "heart" vs. " shoulder" is very small. And it is even more difficult for panicked, not-highly-trained individuals in dangerous, stressful situations.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.9.1.2. Pro: Other than the head and chest, most people would not know where to aim for vital arteries that will cause the assailant to bleed out quickly enough to stop them from being a threat.  Although you should be prepared to shoot if you draw a weapon, you may not be required to.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.9.1.3. Pro: Only wounding an attacker may not stop the attack.  If the attacker has enough adrenaline, or is on drugs, or possibly just does not react to pain the way most people do, they may continue to attack if they are only wounded.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.9.2. Con: Even if you are able to fire at the legs in a stressful situation, the legs have some major arteries like the femoral artery which would cause someone to bleed out quickly if these arteries are severed.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.9.3. Con: If you only shoot to disable and hit the aggressor but fail to disable or stop them or run them off, you have not only wasted your shot, but possibly worsened the situation because now they are angry, hyped up on adrenaline, and potentially more dangerous than they were.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.10. Pro: You can fire your gun at the vital organs of the aggressor \(head/torso\).
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.10.1. Con: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.9.1.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.11. Pro: You can choose more-lethal or less-lethal rounds.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.11.1. Pro: Hollowpoints are specifically designed to cause more tissue damage.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.11.1.1. Con: There is no reasonable justification for civilian use of these.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.11.1.1.1. Con: It can take multiple bullets to stop an attacker. Hollow points reduce the number of hits needed to make sufficient tissue damage to stop an attacker. Fewer rounds fired results in fewer potential innocent bystanders getting shot.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.11.1.1.2. Con: Hunters could use hollow points to take down game more quickly.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.11.2. Pro: Rubber bullets are also viable less-lethal options, often used for crowd control.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.11.3. Con: This has nothing to do with how an individual responds to a threat in the moment.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.5. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.1.4.9.1.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.2. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.3.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.3. Con: It is worth the risk that some non-lethal attackers die, than the guarantee that all victims of lethal attackers will die without being able to defend themselves with equivalent lethal force.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.4. Pro: The availability of a lethal option allows the possibility of choosing lethal force in a non-lethal scenario.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.4.1. Con: Non-lethal scenarios can become lethal at any time.  A fistfight can become lethal if someone gets knocked out and the attacker decides to kill them while they're unconscious.  However the non-availability of a lethal option does not allow the possibility of choosing lethal force in a lethal scenario.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.9.5. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.5.2.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2. Con: Morality aside it is indefensible to give any human the legal right to decide if another human lives or dies, apart from a few extreme cases \(somebody in physical pain wanting to die maybe\).
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.1. Pro: Self defence should limit itself to situations where the defender did not have a chance to have an outcome without casualties. But that is unfeasible in facts
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.2. Con: This claim presupposes that gun control would get rid of all the guns available, which would never be the case due to the black market, etc.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.2.1. Con: Gun control does not have to be achieved completely to have a positive effect on society. Lowering the amount of guns makes a situation with guns on both ends less and less plausible
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3. Con: Individuals should not be obligated to let themselves be killed if someone is trying to kill them.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.1. Pro: Making it illegal to fight for your life would be immoral and abhorrent under any modern system of morality or criminal justice.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2. Con: If fewer people had the ability to kill someone easily and quickly, it is less likely that any individual would have their life threatened directly.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.1. Con: Life is mortal peril, and as such, anything which is alive is in some form of mortal peril at all times.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2. Con: Guns are not the major form of mortal peril that human beings face from other human beings. Physical violence in all its forms do not decrease under gun control, only the use of guns to enact violence. If a potential victim has no gun and is being threatened by multiple attackers, then that victim is in fact at more likelihood of mortal peril than if they had a gun to defend themselves or deter multiple attackers.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1. Con: The destructive power of a gun is not impacted by the physical strength of the user. If humans are fundamentally violent, then restricting access to guns would restrict their destructive power.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.1. Con: Restricting access to guns for SOME would not restrict the destructive power of ALL, since only some people would not be allowed to own guns.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.1.1. Con: Some would be a start. Targeted action might at least prevent some situations from being deadly.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.1.1.1. Con: Taking guns from some people and not others may only increase the pool of possible victims that are defenseless.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.1.1.1.1. Con: A gun is hardly a defense against somebody wanting to kill you, as unless you carry a gun at all times and have eyes all around you and can take your gun out instantly you are indeed defenseless against somebody coming unexpected anyway.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.1.1.1.1.1. Con: By that logic then there is no difference as to whether a criminal has a gun or not, since they can simply sneak up on someone and kill them anyway with a knife or a rock.  Either way, gun control does not improve the situation for non-criminals.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.2. Pro: Becoming a more dangerous individual is acceptable for society only if you are a sane and responsible individual. Allowing individuals to become more dangerous without any need to verify their sanity and responsibility has a long tray of bad potential outcomes.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3. Pro: The simplicity, ease of access, and destructive power of a firearm makes it more likely that conflict will escalate.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1. Pro: Overall, more guns [correlate](https://www.hsph.harvard.edu/hicrc/firearms-research/guns-and-death/) with more homicide.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.1. Con: If we attempt to correlate total firearm-related deaths per 100,000 population per year with guns per 100 inhabitants \(data available here: [List of countries by firearm death](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_firearm-related_death_rate)\), the value of R is -0.066; a weak negative correlation. As such, the data essentially suggest no correlation between gun ownership and gun deaths.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.1.1. Con: The correlation coefficient you mention is a linear one and does not take into account outliers and leverage points. Moreover, South American countries \(Brazil, Colombia and Guatemala among others\) - whose 'gun death' exceeds 20 - skew the linear correlation towards a negative one.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.1.2. Con: Doing regressions without adjusting for other associated factors - like the functionality of the local police force or the existence of anti-state actors \(e.g. large drug cartels\) - isn't ever going to give an indicative result. This is why actual studies on the correlation between gun ownership and firearm deaths adjust for other established associated factors.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.1.3. Con: Your statistical study is of international statistical correlations, whereas the parent claim makes intra-national correlations. Other countries do not share our Constitution, history, and culture. Therefore the correlation coefficient will naturally be weaker as our differences are too complex to be statistically controlled.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.1.4. Con: Firearm related deaths per 100,000 people in the US are 11.96 per the source quoted.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.2. Con: Where firearms are most dense violent crime rates are [lowest](http://www.law.harvard.edu/students/orgs/jlpp/Vol30_No2_KatesMauseronline.pdf), and where guns are least dense violent crime rates are highest.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.2.1. Con: The paper in question [was published in an ideological student law review \(not a peer-reviewed journal\), did not involve any actual research, and has been widely debunked as misrepresenting the conclusions of the actual studies it discusses](https://www.snopes.com/harvard-flaw-review/).
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.2.1.1. Pro: In particular, its claim that studies had found evidence that gun control did not work to reduce crime misrepresented the conclusions of those studies, which were rather concluding that there were grounds for further research due to a lack of empirical studies necessary to draw conclusions.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.2.2. Pro: Similar conclusions have been found by [Plassman and Tideman](http://www.journals.uchicago.edu/doi/abs/10.1086/323311) \(2001\), [Helland and Tabarrok](http://crimeresearch.org/wp-content/uploads/2015/03/Helland-Tabarrok-Placebo-Laws.pdf) \(2004\), and the notorious work of Lott.  It is important to distinguish in such a statement the difference between citizens with firearms and criminals with firearms.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.3. Pro: If guns in society increased safety, then US gun death rates would be lower than places where there are gun restrictions. [Instead](https://www.cbsnews.com/news/how-u-s-gun-deaths-compare-to-other-countries/), they are comparatively very high. Therefore, guns in society do not increase safety.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.3.1. Con: There are varying degrees of accuracy in how these numbers are calculated.  Some rank the US as high as number 11, others dipping down to 50 something.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.4. Pro: The correlation [holds true among US states](http://archive.sph.harvard.edu/press-releases/2007-releases/press01112007.html) as well - states with higher rates of gun ownership have higher rates of both firearm homicide and homicide in general, once other factors \(wealth, urbanisation, etc\) are controlled for.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.4.1. Con: Ignoring all of the factors that actually contribute to increased homicide \(poverty, urban population density, etc.\) in order to skew the data towards blaming guns is not going to produce a valid conclusion. It'd be like saying "Chicago has a really low murder rate, once you control for the factors of gangs and drug related crimes."
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.4.2. Pro: It is important to control for these factors, as otherwise locations that for various known reasons are more or less susceptible to crime in general, for reasons independent of gun ownership, skew the data.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.4.2.1. Con: Rather than making the data fit arguments for increased gun control, we should address these factors that contribute to crime in general.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5. Pro: Other industrialized countries have gun control and they have lower gun murder rates. It is important to note that gun control doesn't mean "no guns" - it means not certain kinds of guns.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.1. Pro: In 2012, in the US, the number of gun murders per capita was nearly 30 times that in the UK.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.2. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.4.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3. Pro: Australia has managed to greatly reduce the number of firearms in public hands \(almost completely eliminated\) through buy-back incentives and other programs. The implementation of similar incentives could also be applied in the US.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.1. Con: The US is larger, containing around 325 million guns. Even if the [Australian plan](https://youtu.be/wAXxQBIfH7I?t=1m13s) was tried and worked to perfection, you'd still be left with over 200 million guns in the US.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.1.1. Pro: Comparing two countries without considering all other social, cultural, and economic characteristics isn't a solid reasoning to support a conclusion.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2. Con: Gun control [has not](http://www.theage.com.au/interactive/2016/gun-city/day1.html) been effective in Australia.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2.1. Con: The underlying report cited notes a recorded rate of shootings of 99 in 20 months. The Gun Violence Archive, which documents incidents in the US, records 58,799 incidents in 2016 - even accounting for relative population size, Australia's regime is clearly working better to limit the total rate of gun violence.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2.2. Con: The report quoted shows gun homicide numbers usually below 10 for the whole state. That's pretty darn effective.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2.3. Con: While there are reasons to be concerned about gaps in the laws and their enforcement, the general expert conclusion is that they were [incredibly effective](https://cdn1.sph.harvard.edu/wp-content/uploads/sites/1264/2012/10/bulletins_australia_spring_2011.pdf).
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2.4. Pro: Australia's homicide rate has been [dropping](http://www.aic.gov.au/media_library/publications/mr/mr23/mr23.pdf) steadily for [decades](http://www.aic.gov.au/statistics/homicide.html). They enacted a gun buyback program that caused a substantial drop in gun ownership there. Afterwards, gun ownership rose again as [citizens rearmed](http://sydney.edu.au/news/84.html?newsstoryid=10824), to the point that the original buyback was eclipsed in 2013. The homicide rate has continued its steady decline, with no statistically significant influence from either event.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2.4.1. Con: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2.3.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2.5. Con: While the rate of gun crime has increased since laws were first strengthened in 1996, this more reflects [the erosion of Australia's gun control regime](http://www.smh.com.au/nsw/former-prime-minister-john-howard-slams-erosion-of-gun-control-laws-20150908-gjhqhd.html), rather than inherent flaws in its original design.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2.6. Pro: According to Australia's own study on the matter \(outdated, 2007\) "It does not appear that the Australian experience with gun buybacks is fully replicable in the United 
States."See Section 4, "Conclusion." [cdn1.sph.harvard.edu](https://cdn1.sph.harvard.edu/wp-content/uploads/sites/1264/2012/10/bulletins_australia_spring_2011.pdf)
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2.6.1. Con: "fully" is the key word. They are two incredibly different countries.  But the full text of the conclusion provides a different view: "... Levitt provides three reasons why gun buybacks in the United States have apparently been ineffective: \(a\) the buybacks are relatively small in scale \(b\) guns are surrendered voluntarily, and so are not like the ones used in crime; and \(c\) replacement guns are easy to obtain. These factors did not apply to the Australian buyback ..."
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2.6.1.1. Con: OK, sure, but \(a\) is true BECAUSE there's little interest in surrendering firearms; \(b\) is true--the ones that are surrendered are junk; and \(c\) is an unalterable condition. 

Guns are plentiful, well understood and easy to manufacture at high quality using common shop tools. 

Prohibiting them is unlikely to be well received by the 100 Million+ citizens who own them, so enforcement is difficult and ease of manufacture means criminals will have access, which is a big reason people buy guns.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2.7. Pro: Australia now has [more firearms](http://www.abc.net.au/news/2016-04-28/australia-has-more-guns-than-before-port-arthur-massacre/7366360) in public possession than before the buyback.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2.8. Con: Australia: [More Firearms Now But Less Gun Crime](http://www.abc.net.au/news/2016-04-28/fact-check-gun-homicides-and-suicides-john-howard-port-arthur/7254880) 
Responsible gun ownership is the result of the restrictions placed 22 years ago. The restrictions have proven extremely effective because [responsible gun owners](http://time.com/4172274/what-its-like-to-own-guns-in-a-country-with-strict-gun-control/) can still own them if they want to. While some criminals are heavily armed \(as it happens in every country in the world\), the public is generally not shot by them [because the public is generally unarmed](https://www.psychologytoday.com/us/blog/get-psyched/201301/the-weapons-effect). The homicide rate continues to drop in spite of a growing population.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.3. Pro: In the 18 years prior to gun law reforms, Australia had [13](https://www.google.com.au/amp/amp.slate.com/blogs/the_slatest/2017/10/03/did_gun_control_stop_mass_shootings_in_australia_probably.html) mass shootings before the government passed legislation that greatly restricted the use of, ownership of, and availability of fire arms. Since the 1996 reforms, there have been none. In a developed democratic countries, gun laws are effective.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.3.1. Con: [There have been several](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_massacres_in_Australia) mass shootings since then \(the Hunt family killings, the Sydney siege, etc\). Taking into account the other massacres that take place \(arson attacks/etc. which often have higher body counts than the mass shooting attacks\), the average number of Australians killed by massacres has not gone down.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.3.1.1. Con: The Sydney siege resulted in [one person](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Sydney_hostage_crisis) being killed by the assailant - that's not a massacre. The police killed the other victim with a ricochet, as well as killing the assailant.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.3.1.1.1. Pro: This was, in part, because all the shooter could get to carry out his massacre was a sawn-off shotgun with four shots.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.3.1.1.2. Con: The deaths weren't kept to a minimum because he had a shotgun, \(watch [this video](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z3m-WNk44hI) to see how effective they can be\) they were kept to a minimum because police shot him as soon as he started killing people.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.4. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2.3.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.5. Con: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2.7.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.6. Con: Australia reduced the number of guns legally owned by the public, but the black market has steadily been growing leading to more and more criminals being armed \(and then using those weapons to commit crimes\).
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.6.1. Con: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2.3.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.6.2. Con: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.3.2.5.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.4. Con: Gun murder rate is irrelevant. The murder rate is what's important. Addressing one without the other leads to misleading arguments along the lines of: "Toyota is the most common car in America.  The rate of drunk driving deaths in the US involving Toyota Camrys is far higher than the rate involving Toyotas in Cuba, where they do not have them.  Therefore banning Toyota in the US will save lives."
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.4.1. Con: This draws illogical parallels. The Toyota brand is not itself a means of transportation any more than the Winchester brand is a means of shooting, and nobody is trying to ban one specific brand of firearm. We regulate *all* vehicles and their usage to prevent or mitigate the risks vehicular homicide, for the same reason that *all* firearms and their usage should be regulated to prevent or mitigate the risks of firearm homicide.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.4.1.1. Con: Toyota wasn't used as a brand in the analogy, think of Toyota as guns and other brands of cars as other weapons.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.4.2. Con: This utterly avoids the question of whether access to a gun increases the likelihood of committing murder or suicide. Evidence [strongly](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-gun-suicide/gun-access-tied-to-greater-suicide-murder-risk-study-idUSBREA0J1G920140120) indicates that it does.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.4.2.1. Con: The [Reuters source](https://www.reuters.com/article/us-gun-suicide/gun-access-tied-to-greater-suicide-murder-risk-study-idUSBREA0J1G920140120) has problems. It uses studies published from 1988 - 2005. Since then, homicide rates have declined significantly, at the same time the number of guns has [increased](https://mises.org/wire/fbi-us-homicide-rate-51-year-low). There also doesn't seem to be connection to suicide and gun ownership [rates](https://www.psychologytoday.com/us/blog/the-new-brain/201607/fact-check-gun-control-and-suicide).
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.5. Con: Correlation does not imply causation. America is a completely different animal that has many different problems \(racial conflict, mental illness, etc.\) that other developed countries do not.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.5.5.1. Con: Since the US is a country with more racial conflict, more mental illness, etc., shouldn't we limit our guns or our gun types? Handguns are designed to kill people - whether through self-defense or not.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.6. Con: The number of guns in circulation has increased steadily in the US for decades during which violent crime rates, including gun crime, has steadily [decreased](http://www.aei.org/publication/chart-of-the-day-more-guns-less-gun-violence-between-1993-and-2013/).
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.6.1. Con: Correlation based reasoning is good for some domains but not for politics.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.6.1.1. Pro: General crime statistics are not as relevant as the crises we have witnessed as a result of mentally unstable people acting out against the public and being effectively lethal in doing so due to having access to firearms. Such individuals are difficult to pick out of a crowd or any specific demographic, thus making targeted restrictions difficult to implement.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.6.1.2. Pro: A politic could be defined by a pack of answers to questions that start by "how should we deal with ..." "what to do if ... happens" and politics would be about taking those systems and seeing what effect they have. A politic that has more guns in it could be very good or very bad depending on what the other answers to the other questions are.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.6.1.3. Con: If pro-gun control arguments use a correlative approach, then it is sensible to counter that approach with a similar counter-claim. "More guns = more crime = more death", contrasted with "actually we have more guns and yet less crime and less death" is entirely logical and sensible as a rebuttal to this claim.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.6.1.3.1. Pro: Correlation is acceptable as an argument as long as both parties agree about the period of the data,and veracity of the sources. These are complex issues and any correlation will be based on multiple hidden variables, so neither party should read too much into it..
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.6.2. Con: This has more to do with the overall [general decrease](https://www.statista.com/statistics/191219/reported-violent-crime-rate-in-the-usa-since-1990/) in violent crime in the U.S. There are [many theories](https://www.vox.com/cards/crime-rate-drop) for why this happened, but most researchers have [concluded there](https://www.vox.com/cards/crime-rate-drop/guns-prevent-crime) is no reason to think that guns deserve credit for the crime decline.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.6.2.1. Con: Correlation is not necessarily causation, that's true and works on both sides of this issue. However, while guns may not be conclusively credited for the decline, the fact that the violent crime/murder rates have decreased dramatically faster than many places which either did not have many guns, or who banned them during that same time period, pretty strongly indicates that the notion that guns are the source of violence is false.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.6.2.1.1. Con: Guns are indeed not the source of violence but guns heavily aggravate the potential damage which could be inflicted and the range/area of effect both.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.6.2.1.1.1. Con: Cars or trucks can also heavily aggravate the potential damage of violence
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.6.2.1.1.2. Con: Ignoring the root causes will only allow the problem to get worse.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.7. Pro: [In 2007](https://www.jhsph.edu/research/centers-and-institutes/johns-hopkins-center-for-gun-policy-and-research/_pdfs/effects-of-missouris-repeal-of-its-handgun-purchaser-licensing-law-on-homicides.pdf), Missouri repealed its handgun permit law, and immediately saw an increase in firearm murders, but not other types of murders.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.8. Pro: According to [cnbc.com](https://www.cnbc.com/2018/02/27/states-with-strict-gun-laws-have-fewer-firearms-deaths-heres-how-your-state-stacks-up.html) a CDC study and a special project cross-analyzed firearm deaths per state and number of firearm regulations per state, finding a negative correlation \(more regulations correlated with fewer firearm deaths\).
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.9. Con: "Based on the CDC data, almost 60 percent of U.S. firearm homicides occur in the 62 cities of the country’s 50 largest metros." Looking at comparisons state-wide instead of city-wide conceal where the majority of homicides really occur.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.10. Con: These studies often do not distinguish between legal and illegal guns. Crimes are more likely to be committed with guns obtained illegally.  Stricter gun control is much more likely to limit legal gun ownership.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.2. Pro: These are powerful weapons and should be treated with respect.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.3. Pro: Having a gun pointed at you makes you basically surrender automatically, and puts you completely under the power of the person pointing a gun at you, which is a violent experience by itself.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.4. Con: [Mutually Assured Destruction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutual_assured_destruction) actually prevented nuclear conflict during the Cold War \(and continues today\) because of the high potential of casualties and costs to both sides using the most powerful weapons known to man. Destructive power makes conflict more risky, and therefore less likely to occur the more equivalent the power of the tools employed by both sides.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.4.1. Con: This does not apply to individuals. MAD relies on leaders making calculated decisions. Not everyone with a gun or other weapon will be a rational or sensible actor who is afraid of the costs of a fight with guns or otherwise, so the deterrent of equivalent force may not always result in deescalation.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.4.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.3.1.3.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.4.1.2. Con: The vast majority of human beings behave as rational actors with a strong sense of self-preservation that is enough to make two opponents think twice about getting into a conflict that they are both likely to lose.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.4.1.2.1. Con: People's sense of self-preservation is exactly what causes them to misinterpret the threat as more dangerous than it is, which is what causes interpersonal conflicts to unnecessarily escalate.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.4.1.2.2. Con: Modern weaponry can increase the killing potential of any individual, provided they can access weapons that allow them to kill many people quickly.  Ergo, even if the vast majority of human being act rationally, the minority, irrational actors will continue to be increasingly and unnacceptably dangerous and costly to the rest of society - unless access to dangerous weapons is restricted.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.4.1.3. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.1.5.2.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.4.2. Con: Given that America owns nearly 40% of all privately owned firearms in the world \(with \<5% of the world's population\) one should expect the US to have the lowest crime rate of any nation \(as per your hypothesis\). I don't believe this is true \(although I'm happy to edit/delete this claim with refuting evidence...\)
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.5. Pro: Increased right to carry laws [correlate](https://www.theatlantic.com/politics/archive/2017/06/right-to-carry-gun-violence/531297/) with increases in violent crime rates.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.5.1. Con: It's not true. Most studies show that laws suppressing the right to own and carry fire arms results in higher rates of gun violence. [www.gunfacts.info](http://www.gunfacts.info/gun-control-myths/concealed-carry/)
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.6. Con: The ease of access to fists far exceeds that of firearms yet one cannot argue that the availability of fists "makes it more likely that conflict will escalate".
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.6.1. Con: Conflict escalating to fists is far less dangerous than escalating to guns.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.7. Con: There is no correlation between simplicity of firearms and conflict. One is not more likely to attack someone with a simple blunderbuss than a complicated AR-15.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.8. Con: If that were true, given that there are over 100 million legal gun owners, and over 10 million with concealed carry permits \(not counting the constitutional carry states\), the United States would be a bloodbath as millions of people would just be running around shooting everyone in sight over the smallest conflicts. The fact that this does not happen proves that your worry is unfounded.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.8.1. Con: The fact that everyone does not run around shooting people in fact does not prove that access to more lethal weaponry does not increase the chance that people do.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.8.2. Con: Many would indeed perceive the US to be a bloodbath, with the ready access to guns in the cases of infidelity/relationship ending, business disagreement, disgruntlement of employees the cause of much of the violence.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.8.2.1. Con: Perception is not as valid a measure of real societal dynamics as statistics or real facts. Empiricism the most effective and accurate way to determine what is or is not true.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.8.3. Pro: [The US has the highest number of guns per capita](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estimated_number_of_guns_per_capita_by_country), estimated at over 300 Million. If it was the case that more guns = more gun deaths, then the US should therefore also be #1 in gun deaths. In fact, [Honduras is the highest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_firearm-related_death_rate) with 65 gun homicides per 100k people per year, and the US only has 10 gun homicides per 100k people per year. The statement that more guns = more gun deaths cannot therefore be supported.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.8.3.1. Con: The abilities of these two countries to enforce their gun control laws are different.  Using 2016 political stability index from the world bank as a proxy for ability to enforce laws, Croatia had a political stability index of 0.67 \(somewhat stable\) while Honduras had a political stability index of -0.36 \(somewhat unstable\).  Claims that strict gun control laws are not always effective need to look at the ability of a country to enforce such laws.  \(source: [theglobaleconomy.com](https://www.theglobaleconomy.com/rankings/wb_political_stability/)\)
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.8.3.1.1. Pro: The US would not have the ability to reduce the number of guns to a level that UK or Japan has.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.8.3.2. Pro: El Salvador at 109 per 100k is actually higher than Honduras. The US only has 5 per 100k rather than 10.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.4. Con: On that same note, government uses force and the threat of force to compel compliance. Limiting its ability to compel force also limits its potentially destructive nature. It is what our constitution and bill of rights sought to do in laying out the limits of government. Be careful when you seek to undo those limitations for the sake of perceived safety.[That every man be armed](http://www.stephenhalbrook.com/everyman.html)
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.5. Con: The fact that strength, speed, agility and a host of other physical attributes does not make a gun more powerful or deadly is why so many women choose a firearm for self-defense. It levels the playing field and makes their comparative weakness inconsequential.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.6. Con: The fundamental violence of nature is not limited to humans. Humans routinely use firearms to defend against violent naturally occurring foes.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.7. Con: Restricting access to firearms does not reduce the destructive power of humans as evidenced by violent people who use knives or massive vehicles to impart similar or greater destructive power on their targets.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.8. Con: If humans are fundamentally violent, why are peaceable interactions between people more common than violent ones?
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.3. Con: Most mass murders in history have been committed by governments against unarmed populations in their own [countries](http://www.dailyherald.com/article/20130127/discuss/701279952/).
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.3.1. Con: There is absolutely [no evidence](https://whistlinginthewind.org/2014/03/05/the-genocide-and-gun-control-myth/) that gun control precipitates nor enables a totalitarian government. In fact, many totalitarian governments \(Stalin, Mao\) came to power via rebellions by armed civilians.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.3.1.1. Con: Ordinary Soviet and Chinese citizens were not allowed to own firearms.  The regimes may have risen to power on the arms of their supporters, but they disarmed most citizens after attaining power.  The people had no way  to oppose them and were so terrified that they would turn in their parents, spouse, or children to avoid being punished themselves if their family member was caught. [look at section about footsteps](https://www.washingtonpost.com/graphics/2017/world/north-korea-defectors/?utm_term=.6f9142640322)
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.3.1.2. Con: [The writings of the Chinese Communist Party](https://books.google.com/books?id=op3sCwAAQBAJ&pg=PT456&dq=Inspecting+for+and+Banning+of+Privately+Owned+Firearms&hl=en&sa=X&ved=0ahUKEwjWs6umxsPdAhVG3IMKHTa3Aq4Q6AEIJzAA#v=onepage&q=Inspecting%20for%20and%20Banning%20of%20Privately%20Owned%20Firearms&f=false) specifically call for the disarmament of anyone that is not a member of the party and in a recognized militia. The [Council of People's Commissars passed an act in 1918](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gun_laws_in_the_Soviet_Union) ordering the removal of all weapons from private hands regardless of their serviceability. The only exception was Communist Party members who were allowed a single pistol or rifle. So Stalin and Mao allowed guns for their supporters until they were in power, then took them away.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.3.1.3. Pro: There are more examples of an armed citizen rebellion leading to totalitarian governments than leading to free democratic societies.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.3.1.3.1. Pro: The French revolution led to Napoleon's empire, which had perhaps more state control than the old regime.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.3.1.3.2. Pro: The repressive [Castro regime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_Revolution) in Cuban came to power via armed rebellion.
1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.3.1.3.3. Pro: The [Iranian government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Revolution) came to power via armed rebellion.

1.2.5.1.1.1.2. Pro: Guns are weapons, not toys. They were designed for one purpose: to kill. If people want to "play" with guns, they can use items specifically designed for that purpose. Options include paintball guns, BB guns, pellet guns, and airsoft guns.
1.2.5.1.1.1.2.1. Con: Guns are designed to fire a projectile through the barrel within a  degree of accuracy. There are numerous options from rubber bullets to other non-lethal projectiles. Intent of the user would be to kill, not the inanimate object. As an analog, certain knives are designed specifically to cut meat, human or animal depends on the user, not designer.
1.2.5.1.1.1.2.2. Con: Guns are not toys, however that does not preclude recreational and sporting use of firearms. There are multiple Olympic shooting events, for example.  Target shooting improves overall skill level and reinforces gun safety.
1.2.5.1.1.1.2.2.1. Pro: The gun restrictions could be designed with this in mind. For example, the guns used could stay at the shooting ground.
1.2.5.1.1.1.2.2.1.1. Con: Some people feel safer when they have a gun in their house.
1.2.5.1.1.1.2.3. Con: Whether a gun is a weapon or a toy depends on the usage, not the purpose or design. Whether guns "should" be used as toys is a different matter.
1.2.5.1.1.1.3. Con: The fact that people want to 'play' with firearms does not mean they should be equated with toys. The primary purpose of a toy is to entertain and educate a child. The primary purpose of a firearm is to even the odds against a life threatening assailant or assailants.
1.2.5.1.1.1.4. Pro: If guns were not designed to kill, they would not be effective or desirable as self-defense tools.
1.2.5.1.1.1.5. Con: Some people also own guns for sport - hunting, shooting clay pigeons, target practice at the range, etc.  Would you prohibit these activities?
1.2.5.1.1.1.6. Con: Guns can prevent or stop crimes without killing someone if the user is prepared to actually use them and the assailant is aware of the intent. The assailant may be chased off or stopped and held for police. Police officers carry guns daily but do not shoot on a daily basis or in each encounter with criminals.
1.2.5.1.2. Con: Note that murder is banned, not the tools used to carry it out, because we cannot consider "the ability to do something bad" as something bad in and of itself without criminalizing literally everything.
1.2.5.1.2.1. Con: Many tools that can be used to kill someone, like chemical weapons and poisons, because they make it easy to carry out the act. It's in the interest of the public health to tightly regulate things that make killing people easy.
1.2.5.1.2.1.1. Con: Once you accept some limitations - for example, on automatic weapons - those are then used as a rationale for further restrictions, eventually leading to a complete ban.
1.2.5.1.2.1.1.1. Con: Restrictions do not necessarily lead to bans. There are restrictions on cars, programming, food, and others, without an outright ban on any of them. There are shades of acceptance between 'outright ban' and 'outright acceptance', and as a society it's up to us to figure out where that line is, and when necessary change it.
1.2.5.2. Con: However, this would allow police to confiscate weapons from criminals with far, far greater ease.

What results is, criminals find it more difficult to obtain guns and gun crime is reduced dramatically. 1.2.8. Pro: There are too many guns in America. Americans own more guns per capita more than any other country. According to the Congressional Research Service, Americans own [nearly half](https://www.cnn.com/2017/10/03/americas/us-gun-statistics/index.html) of the world's civilian-owned guns, although we are only 5% of the world's population.
1.2.8.1. Con: The number of guns owned within the U.S. as compared to other countries is irrelevant.  If we say that the U.S. has put infinitely more people on the moon than any other country, it's no evidence of an actual problem.
