1.2.8.1.1.2. Con: Many nations with fewer guns available have higher intentional homicide rates.
1.2.8.1.1.3. Con: Gun violence is not precisely our concern; preventing violence of all kinds is our goal.
1.2.8.1.1.3.1. Pro: By framing the issue narrowly as one of gun violence, it becomes easy to entertain proposals which may reduce gun violence specifically, yet lead to even greater increases in other kinds of violence.
1.2.8.1.1.3.2. Pro: This is precisely correct. Just because we see that gun deaths are an issue at large does not mean that gun deaths are the only problem. Out of the top 10 leading causes of death in the US, the only gun related item was suicide at number 10, and not all suicides are performed with guns. 8 of the 9 items above suicide on the list are heath-related like heart disease and cancer, while the number 4 item on the list is accidents \(the article refers to cars specifically\).
1.2.8.1.1.4. Con: The amount of available guns versus the amount of gun deaths are actually reverse of what the parent claim is implying. According to [two AEI graphs](http://fortysixnews.com/stories/2015/12/06/stats-show-more-guns-equals-less-gun-violence-between-1993-and-2013/), the amount of gun homicides in the US have actually gone down over the studied 20 year period as gun ownership has gone up.
1.2.8.1.1.5. Con: Correlation does not equal causation. Just because gun ownership is going up does not mean that, as a direct result of that, the gun death rate is going up.
1.2.8.1.2. Pro: The USA is different to its developed nation peers in many other ways than simply gun ownership. To assume that gun ownership is the deciding factor in the USA's relatively high levels of violent crime disregards other possible factors, like gang activity or racial tensions.
1.2.8.1.3. Con: The amount of people that we put on the moon and the amount of guns in circulation have nothing to do with each other. Guns can actually cause harm and kill, while putting people on the moon is a great accomplishment of mankind. While the "number of guns owned" argument is indeed irrelevant, it is not at all comparable to the amount of people on the moon
1.2.8.2. Con: Americans own more guns per capita but are not the highest in gun violence. The US is actually closer to the [lowest](https://www.npr.org/sections/goatsandsoda/2017/10/06/555861898/gun-violence-how-the-u-s-compares-to-other-countries) \(This is a link from the background of the debate. Look closely as the scales of the graph are different and can be deceiving\). US is also not even close to the highest homicide rate. Again we are much closer to the [lowest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_intentional_homicide_rate).
1.2.8.2.1. Con: On the linked list, the US is 126th in murder rate out of 219 countries, directly between Kazakhstan and Kyrgyzstan. For context, the United Kingdom's 37th ranked rate is 5.3 times smaller than the US's. There is no world where the US is more comparable developmentally and societally to Kazakhstan and Kyrgyzstan than the UK.
1.2.8.2.1.1. Con: The US is 126th out of 219 countries however the homicide rate goes from nearly 0 to 109 per 100,000. The US is around 5 per 100,000. Considering the scale, we are much closer to the lowest. We have a low homicide rate and by far the most guns per [capita](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estimated_number_of_guns_per_capita_by_country). More guns don't mean more homicides. If it did, these two charts would be somewhat correlated.
1.2.8.2.1.2. Con: Kazakhstan and Kyrgyzstan both have somewhat low intentional homicide rates at around 5 per 100,000 per year.
1.2.8.2.1.3. Con: The UK counts murders only if someone is charged with a [crime](http://igeek.com/w/U.S._vs_U.K._-_Crime/Murder). The US uses two [methods](https://www.bjs.gov/content/pub/pdf/ntmh.pdf) which provides a more detailed picture and counts murders even when no one is charged with a crime.
1.2.8.2.2. Con: The resource does not support the claim as it shows "homicide rates" not gun violence rates. It is not representative of gun violence statistics. According to gun violence statistics US is next to Uruguay, Mexico and Argentina. They are preceded only by countries that are known for ongoing internal conflicts.  [en.wikipedia.org](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_firearm-related_death_rate)
1.2.8.2.2.1. Con: It is important to look at thing such as homicide rates rather than only gun violence statistics. Many times, violent people who don't have access to guns, simply use other weapons to kill. Without considering homicides that don't use guns, it would be impossible to know if guns actually make a society more violent or if people simply use other weapons. It appears to be the latter. Increased gun ownership does not increase homicide rates as the two metrics aren't even correlated.
1.2.8.3. Con: The number of guns in America is completely irrelevant. It's the same as every other God-given right we have. You could just as easily say "there are too many newspapers in America." The government \(and the populace\) has no right to determine what is "too many." That's a judgmental and arbitrary opinion, which has no effect on the legal status of guns, and holds no logical weight. There are also "too many obese people" in America. Should we "ban obesity" as well?
1.2.9. Con: Stricter regulation adversely and disproportionately affects low-income citizens, who often are more likely do be potential victims of violence, with application fees and often a necessity to take time off work to complete the necessary steps to comply with regulation.
1.2.10. Con: The primary [purposes of law](http://www.businesslawbasics.com/chapter-3-purposes-and-functions-law-1) are to establish minimum acceptable standards of behavior, maintain order, resolve disputes, and to protect property and rights. Creating regulations solely for the purpose of making consumers consider decisions about potential purchases 'more carefully' would not aid in any of these primary functions.
1.2.10.1. Pro: Regulations enacting further hurdles in hopes a customer would think carefully about a gun purchase would deal with personal intentions and hopes about someone's motives and reasoning, but would have nothing to do with the acceptable behavior in society of a citizen buying and owning a gun. It would be a form of thought control, not a behavioral control.
1.2.10.2. Pro: Regulations added solely in hopes a citizen with consider purchases carefully does not aid in orderly running society.
1.2.10.3. Pro: Regulations added in the hope a citizen will consider purchases carefully do nothing to protect the property or rights of the citizen.
1.2.10.4. Con: The proposed regulation would not solely make consumers think more carefully about purchasing firearms; it would also create an actual hindrance for many consumers to legally purchase them.
1.2.10.4.1. Con: due to the purpose of law of setting standards of acceptable behavior, to say that create hindrance to the behave of buy legally a firearm is needed or even likely, is to say that the belief that one should buy legally a firearm is not desirable. this fact is in contrary of the goal of law. [www.businesslawbasics.com](http://www.businesslawbasics.com/chapter-3-purposes-and-functions-law-1)
1.2.10.4.1.1. Pro: if law is something to set standards, the belief the this standard is needed or desirable is itself desirable. to say that one has to, in some level, be restricted in his or hers behavior in order to be in accordance with the standard is the same of to oppose the standard. in this case, hindrance to buy guns legally is hindrance to be a in accordance with law itself.
1.2.11. Con: The significant existing laws should be effectively enforced before adding new ones. This may include sharing of data across enforcement agencies and across state lines.
1.2.11.1. Pro: There is poor prosecution of the existing prohibitions on felons in possession of a firearm. Without enforcing existing legislation and studying that effect, adding restrictions to law-abiding gun owners makes little sense.[politifact.com](http://www.politifact.com/wisconsin/statements/2013/feb/03/mayors-against-illegal-guns/us-files-criminal-charges-fraction-gun-denial-case/). In addition, those felons who are physically caught with a firearm face poor indictment rates.[fox6now.com](http://fox6now.com/2016/10/27/theres-no-disincentive-to-carry-a-gun-felons-with-guns-still-dodge-minimum-sentence-despite-new-law/)
1.2.11.2. Pro: Individual citizens must hold their elected representatives accountable in order to see actual enforcement of [current laws](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gun_laws_in_the_United_States_by_state).
1.2.11.3. Con: Enforcing existing regulations while strengthening and adding additional qualifications are not mutually exclusive.  As such, this isn't an argument against.
1.2.12. Con: If someone is not taking buying a gun seriously, then they, without a doubt, have some sort of mental ailment. Anyone in their right mind should know that guns have the capability of killing a human being with the pull of a trigger, and that keeping a gun is a HUGE responsibility. If someone is suspicious of having a mental ailment or intending harm \(which could be identified by their flippant attitude towards the topic of owning a gun\) should be reported to the police. See the Parkland Shooting
1.2.12.1. Con: Women are more likely to have a [mental ailment](http://ramh.org/guide/gender-differences-in-mental-health/), but they are [less likely to own a gun](http://www.pewsocialtrends.org/2017/06/22/the-demographics-of-gun-ownership/). Only 2% of [mass shootings](https://www.statista.com/statistics/476445/mass-shootings-in-the-us-by-shooter-s-gender/) are done by women, so mental illnesses are not linked to gun violence. But, the possession of guns is.
1.2.13. Con: The decision of whether or not to own a gun has no effect on society.  It is the decisions made subsequent to that purchase that effect society.
1.2.14. Con: when you expand that statement, it takes on different meaning. “Stricter regulations would make -law abiding- people consider their decision to own a gun -for protection against criminals,- more seriously.” This is the same approach that some states take with abortion; because they can’t outlaw abortion, they make the mother see a baby through an ultra sound before she can abort it \(barbaric\). Making a person experience discomfort to prevent them exercising a legal right is not good government.
1.2.15. Pro: Adopting gun laws would not outlaw guns - it would simply make them harder to get. If you really want a gun, you can have one, provided that you get a license and go through all the legal hoops.
1.2.15.1. Con: The only problem with this idea is that some government bureaucrat that doesn't like guns can decide not to allow you to have one. [We see this quite often in "May Issue" states for concealed carry and Firearm Owner ID cards where a person must justify their desire to own a gun.](https://www.thetruthaboutguns.com/2017/02/robert-farago/hawaii-zero-concealed-carry-permits-issues-since-2000/)
1.2.16. Con: Creating more gun regulations will not change cultural perceptions around guns. Policy is generally downstream of culture. Take drug laws in the USA for example - although Marijuana is a [Schedule 1 controlled substance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Controlled_Substances_Act#Schedule_I_controlled_substances) at the federal level, many people use it recreationally despite it being a federal crime. In response, [many](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cannabis_in_California) [states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cannabis_in_Colorado) have legalized its use. The culture around drugs supersedes the regulation.
1.2.16.1. Pro: The legality or illegality of an action does not inherently make it good or bad, wrong or right, just or unjust. There are many examples of laws which were later decided to be immoral \(e.g. the [Tea Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tea_Act), [fugitive slave laws](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fugitive_slave_laws), [Jim Crow laws](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Crow_laws), etc\). The founders of this country itself knew that the [laws of nature supersede all, and laws of man can become tyrannical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence#Annotated_text_of_the_engrossed_declaration). The founders even committed treason in order to "[throw off such Government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right_of_revolution)".
1.2.16.2. Con: Cultural use and habit does not change whether an action is legal or illegal, nor give it any extra ethical or moral weight or justification. Culture does not give legal, much less moral, impetus.
1.2.17. Pro: Enacting waiting periods to purchase guns means that people can not obtain a weapon while particularly enraged.
1.2.18. Pro: Regulations are how states express approval and disapproval. Thus they act as a signal as to what society approves and disapproves of.
1.2.18.1. Pro: Tighter regulations imply that society wants less of that thing, such as tighter restrictions on smoking. Looser regulations imply that society wants more of that thing, such as reducing regulations on oil drilling in order to spur more oil production.
1.2.18.2. Con: -> See 1.2.16.
1.2.18.3. Pro: Laws shape culture, culture shapes laws. Our current culture is perceiving our laws differently than it used to, and many members of society are calling for change. If there is a change in the laws our grandchildren may grow up with a different exposure to gun culture than we did. If the laws stay the same, sides of our culture will likely clash more and more.
1.2.18.3.1. Con: The gun culture in America is overwhelmingly tied to responsible gun ownership rather than using them in harmful ways, i.e. shooting innocent people is denounced but protecting innocent life is praised. Of the [390 million](https://www.thetruthaboutguns.com/2015/12/dean-weingarten/2015-guns-numbers/) privately owned firearms in the US, the vast majority are used lawfully. "Gun culture" in America is positive. Any negative effects of firearms come from neglecting the culture of respecting guns and using them responsibly.

Laws do not make people suddenly think that something is taboo, it is more likely that guns were more of a taboo subject before the laws were passed.

1.3. Pro: Having fewer guns in circulation means society is generally safer.

Con: Registration can \(and has\) led to confiscation of guns/accessories that have later been banned, making civil disobedience in the face of government overreach more likely to result in either serious conflict between gun owners and law enforcement when they [refuse to comply](https://hudsonvalleyone.com/2016/07/07/massive-noncompliance-with-safe-act/)with things like "assault weapon" bans \(after having registered as owners of the newly banned guns\), or a major erosion of [constitutional rights](http://www.rcmp-grc.gc.ca/cfp-pcaf/fs-fd/will-testament-eng.htm).
1.3.1.1.1.1. Pro: The policy would lead to civil war. Many would refuse to turn over their property even for "market value". 1.3.1.1.1.1.1. Con: The US has an army and can handle an armed civil war. The army is much more well prepared and well equipped than any group of individuals and their only issue would be solving such a conflict without casualties. Gun owners not surrendering would make themselves criminals.

1.3.1.1.1.1.3.4. Con: Gun owners are making no demands except that they be left alone to exercise their rights.
1.3.1.1.1.1.3.5. Con: There is nothing just or moral in surrendering to mob tyranny. The United States is not a "majority-rules" democracy, but is a representative republic which uses the separation of powers to maintain a balance between the will of the majority and the inalienable rights of all. If the majority wishes to alienate an inalienable right from the people, this is an illegitimate act of political aggression that would be justly resisted by self-defense against a corrupt majority.
1.3.1.1.1.1.3.6. Con: This equivalent to saying that if the majority does not like something that it should be banned. If the majority decides to reinstate slavery then it should be allowed. However having guns in the hands of the populace could be a deterrent to this type of tyranny.
1.3.1.1.1.1.4. Pro: Forcibly enacting gun control may indeed trigger a civil conflict, just as it triggered the Revolutionary War against the British Empire. Should civil war occur, the body count of that conflict could be thousands of times greater than the annual rate of deaths from gun crimes, terrorism, accidents, and suicides combined. It would not be worth the risk simply by the comparative rise in death toll alone.
1.3.1.1.2. Pro: A better registry would make it easier to trace and identify stolen guns, making it more likely that illegal gun traffickers dealing in stolen weapons are caught.
1.3.1.1.2.1. Pro: When stolen weapons are used in crimes, it can take [months](https://www.vice.com/en_ca/article/wdbd9y/the-atfs-nonsensical-non-searchable-gun-databases-explained-392) to trace them to their origins, because of the lack of a searchable database - or even centralised record-keeping. Cutting this time to hours or even minutes would make it significantly easier to link together information about where weapons came from, and who might have trafficked them.
1.3.1.1.3. Pro: Registry is not in itself a threat upon civil rights. We have the natural right to life, and yet our very lives are registered from the moment we are born in the form of birth certificates to the moment we die in the form of death certificates, with social security numbers, state IDs, etc. in between.
1.3.1.2. Con: An increase in price / cost / burden of ownership would reduce the demand, at least for potential owners without a specific need or particularly strong interest in guns. The percentage of household with guns should therefore continue to diminish.
1.3.1.3. Con: Requiring a permitted purpose for owning a firearm functionally limits the number of firearms someone can lawfully own. Some previously law-abiding people may break the law by keeping more than the allowed limits, but they could then be prosecuted and their gun confiscated. This would reduce the number of guns in circulation.
1.3.1.4. Pro: Many of the guns currently owned by law-abiding citizens may end up in less law-abiding people's hands if the burden of ownership is raised. The buy-back program could help but some people may not want to sell guns to the government.
1.3.1.4.1. Con: If someone is genuinely a law-abiding citizen, it's unclear why they'd choose to seek out a blackmarket sale over participating in a buyback scheme.
1.3.1.4.1.1. Con: In the case of some collectors, to ensure that the weapon will not be scheduled for destruction, especially in the case of \(sub\)machine guns and assault rifles that predate the AR15, or have been used in wars.
1.3.1.4.1.1.1. Con: If the weapons have historical value, museums will happily take them.
1.3.1.4.1.2. Con: The government won't pay enough according to gun owners. They will expect prices above what they paid for in the first place.
1.3.1.4.1.3. Con: Sheer spite of a gun grabbing government is enough of a reason for some.
1.3.1.4.1.4. Pro: Selling a gun on the black market requires significant interaction with serious criminal elements, something that most law-abiding people seek to avoid.
1.3.1.4.1.4.1. Pro: Given a physical transaction is needed, this includes the risk that the person you're selling to will simply catch you off guard and rob you.
1.3.1.4.1.4.2. Con: It's not always the case thet most people avoid criminal elements. If there is a big enough influence of maffia, criminal gangs and corruption it will eventually be normal to interact with them [a.k.a oligarchy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oligarchy).
1.3.1.4.1.5. Pro: Selling a gun on the black market is hardly easy - one can't just put an ad on Craigslist. Such potential vendors would need to know where to go in order to do so without being caught by the police.
1.3.1.4.1.5.1. Con: Tor is readily available and can be downloaded by anyone with a computer, it is a web browser that allows you to see encrypted websites that otherwise would be blocked by regular browsers. Although it takes some time to learn even the most novice user can easily find a site to buy guns by using one of the online directories offered. Sites like SilkRoad still exist and have many users around the world and are as easy to use as Amazon.
1.3.1.4.1.5.1.1. Con: [The founder of SilkRoad went to prison, and the creators of SilkRoad 2.0 went to prison](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silk_Road_\(marketplace\)). The FBI, Interpol, and the UK's National Crime Agency all have dark web task forces. While you can buy a gun online illegally, there is significantly more risk than the parent seems to indicate.
1.3.1.5. Con: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.5.
1.3.2. Pro: Over 230,000 guns are [stolen](https://www.bjs.gov/content/pub/press/fshbopc0510pr.cfm) each year on average from unsecured homes and cars according to the Bureau of Justice Statistics. These guns are a major source for criminals. With strict storage requirements, required reporting of stolen weapons, and fines for having unsecured weapons stolen or not reported if stolen, we could reduce the number of illegally acquired weapons on the street dramatically.
1.3.2.1. Con: There are over 300 million guns in the US. 230,000 thefts accounts for .07 percent of the guns owned by law abiding citizens.
1.3.2.1.1. Con: That’s a quarter of a million armed criminals every year.
1.3.2.1.1.1. Con: This is only true if each criminal only steals one gun and nobody gets more than one stolen gun.
1.3.2.1.2. Con: US guns have been stolen or smuggled in such large numbers that they have been used in large scale conflicts such as the [Mexican drug wars.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Smuggling_of_firearms_into_Mexico)
1.3.2.2. Con: Requiring the reporting of stolen weapons would not help to keep stolen weapons from criminals, rather it would merely create an uptick in the number of weapons reported stolen. This does not achieve more 'safety'.
1.3.2.2.1. Con: People who are required to report the theft of their firearms are more likely to keep better track of them, and store them more securely. If they didn't, their weapons could be stolen and used for a crime before they thought to check upon the weapon's whereabouts.
1.3.2.2.1.1. Pro: [62%](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/wonk/wp/2016/07/27/new-evidence-confirms-what-gun-rights-advocates-have-been-saying-for-a-long-time-about-crime/?utm_term=.760ce0dd0582) of people whose stolen gun was later used in a crime had no idea when or where they lost their firearm.
1.3.2.2.1.1.1. Con: People lose their cars in parking lots often cars are much bigger and more expensive so you would think they would be harder to misplace.  If you keep your guns in a secure location that you do not check every single day, you may not know when someone illegally accessed your storage location.
1.3.2.3. Pro: Most gun owners can legally leave their guns wherever in the household. Only 11 states have laws concerning firearm locking devices \(mostly that a lock must be included in some sales\), only 4 of those states have laws require locking unused firearms at least sometimes, and only 1 state and a handful of cities require the locking of all firearms when not in use.[lawcenter.giffords.org](http://lawcenter.giffords.org/gun-laws/policy-areas/child-consumer-safety/safe-storage/)
1.3.2.4. Pro: If there are fewer guns in circulation, it is more difficult for one to fall into the wrong hands.
1.3.2.4.1. Con: If there are fewer guns in circulation, it is also more difficult for one to be obtained by the right hands.
1.3.2.5. Pro: In the world proposed by this debate, where people must have a specific reason for owning a gun, people are much less likely to be as careless with their guns as they are now.
1.3.2.5.1. Pro: -> See 1.3.2.2.1.1.
1.3.2.6. Con: Strict storage requirements can limit accessibility/usability of a gun in an emergency situation, putting the home's inhabitants at greater risk in case of a violent home invasion.
1.3.2.6.1. Con: Strict storage requirements are generally essential to keeping firearms out of the hands of children, especially toddlers, who kill [roughly a person a week](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/wonk/wp/2015/10/14/people-are-getting-shot-by-toddlers-on-a-weekly-basis-this-year/?utm_term=.98f95def49dc) in the US.
1.3.2.6.1.1. Con: The number of people killed by a toddler is 43 out of 100 million gun owners. People are literally more likely to be [killed by a deer](https://historylist.wordpress.com/2008/05/29/human-deaths-in-the-us-caused-by-animals/), however we don't suggest legislation that requires all cars to be outfitted with anti-deer armor and horn proof glass.
1.3.2.6.1.2. Pro: The report actually only involved a brief search of news reporting, so is likely to be substantially underestimating the true number of incidents. [We do not actually have accurate data](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/post-nation/wp/2014/09/04/how-often-do-children-in-the-u-s-unintentionally-shoot-and-kill-people-we-dont-know/?tid=a_inl&utm_term=.e5c0961c20eb) on the number of shootings carried out by minors, let alone a more nuanced breakdown of that by age.
1.3.2.6.1.3. Con: -> See 1.3.2.3.
1.3.2.6.2. Con: Strict storage requirements also protect gun owners from having their weapons used against them by intruders, family or friends.
1.3.2.6.2.1. Con: -> See 1.3.2.3.
1.3.2.6.3. Con: A gun should not be the only security a person has in their home, and most gun safes can be opened in less than 15 seconds.  If that small amount of time matters, then you've failed in another aspect of security such as locking doors, having a security system.  If a person is too nervous to get the safe open that quickly, then they're also probably too nervous to hit an intruder accurately as well, especially if it's dark.
1.3.2.7. Con: Required reporting of stolen weapons/fines would be completely unenforceable without a gun registry.
1.3.2.8. Con: I think a better solution would be firearm training and education
1.3.3. Con: This is patently false. Take Britain and USA. Many cite gun control for Britain's low homicide rate. But homicides in Britain have been far less than USA long before gun control was enacted.
1.3.3.1. Con: Homicide rates being low to begin with does not necessarily mean that gun control cannot lower them even further.
1.3.3.2. Con: This also reflects the fact that Britain's gun control measures were not enacted in one go. Rather, their initial measures against automatic and semi-automatic weapons were enacted [in the mid-'80s](https://www.washingtonpost.com/world/europe/after-shooting-tragedies-britain-went-after-guns/2013/01/31/b94d20c0-6a15-11e2-9a0b-db931670f35d_story.html?utm_term=.5700d59d045f), before those weapons had a chance to proliferate in the first place.
1.3.3.3. Con: The claim was that society is generally safer. Citing one spurious exception doesn't invalidate the statement. Mass shootings are pretty much non-existent in the UK \(3 in the last century excluding terror related incidents\) but gun crime and gun related homicides are not. They have however dropped drastically since the Firearms Act.
1.3.3.4. Pro: [Great Britain, Ireland, Jamaica, and Australia](https://crimeresearch.org/2013/12/murder-and-homicide-rates-before-and-after-gun-bans/) heavily restricted guns and experienced spikes in incidences of violent crime as a result. Great Britain experienced a 340% increase in violent crime \(including gun violence\). Australia experienced an increase in armed robberies and multiple casualty shootings still occur. The same spikes goes for Ireland and Jamaica. The point is that criminals still find ways to hurt people and a lack of guns disarms people who need to defend themselves.
1.3.4. Pro: The quality of policing would improve if the prevalence of guns were lower.
1.3.4.1. Pro: Police in the US, particularly in states that heavily oppose gun control, [support stricter regulations](https://www.nytimes.com/2016/05/04/us/as-states-expand-gun-rights-police-join-opposition.html).
1.3.4.1.1. Con: That is generally untrue. While some police do, most do not. In New York for example, [virtually every county](http://scopeny.org/Counties_oppose_NYSAFE.html) passed resolutions opposing the NY SAFE act.  They were joined in support by the [NY Sheriff's Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NY_SAFE_Act#cite_note-28), who, while they did not oppose the additional penalties being instated for existing violations, opposed the additional restrictions being placed on New Yorkers and in a number of cases [refused to enforce them](https://www.policeone.com/chiefs-sheriffs/articles/6435415-NY-sheriffs-We-wont-enforce-gun-laws-magazine-limits/).
1.3.4.1.2. Con: No they do not. [Rank and file officers](http://ddq74coujkv1i.cloudfront.net/p1_gunsurveysummary_2013.pdf) are overwhelmingly supportive of 2A rights and so are [their chiefs](http://nacoponline.org/surveyresults.pdf).
1.3.4.1.3. Con: Even if this were true, police are extremely biased on this issue considering that the stricter regulations would almost certainly not apply to them.
1.3.4.2. Pro: When the police know that the potential offender has a high probability of carrying a gun, they are more likely to respond with disproportionate force when they feel threatened.
1.3.4.2.1. Pro: Countries with lower gun ownership have [fewer](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/2015/jun/09/the-counted-police-killings-us-vs-other-countries) police shootings.
1.3.4.2.1.1. Con: Countries with small fractions of the US population have fewer of everything.  Comparing total numbers of police shootings \(as the link does\) between countries with vastly different population sizes and cultures has no statistical merit.
1.3.4.2.1.2. Con: That is obviously not true across the board and is highly dependent on a variety of other factors.  For example, Venezuela has outlawed civilian ownership of guns, and police shoot/kill people there at a rate over [7 times higher](https://www.insightcrime.org/news/analysis/venezuela-police-kill-someone-every-1-5-hours/) than the us.
1.3.4.2.1.3. Con: Some of those countries do not have an armed police force, which bears much more relevance on police shooting statistics than the rate of civilian gun ownership on police shootings.
1.3.4.2.2. Con: If this were true, there would be massively more police shootings/killings in states with loose gun control than in states with strict gun control, however that [isn't what happens](https://mic.com/articles/122161/one-map-shows-all-the-people-police-have-killed-in-each-state-so-far-this-year).
1.3.4.3. Pro: The fact that there are so many guns in circulation is one of the reasons that law enforcement officers are paranoid about traffic stops and makes them more trigger happy. Fewer guns mean police officers don't need to fear for their own safety during a routine stop.
1.3.4.3.1. Con: How many police officers did you poll to come up with this statement?  The former officers I know would often release someone for a minor traffic violation when they showed their \(at the time\) concealed carry license because they knew that this person was not a threat.
1.3.4.3.1.1. Con: [Philando Castile](https://www.nytimes.com/2017/06/16/us/police-shooting-trial-philando-castile.html), a law-abiding Black gun owner, was shot by a police officer while telling the officer he had a legal firearm with him. The NRA has said nothing in support of him.
1.3.4.3.1.1.1. Pro: It is bizarre that a group that seems militantly opposed to any infringement on gun rights would [not defend a person](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/post-nation/wp/2017/06/18/some-gun-owners-are-disturbed-by-the-philando-castile-verdict-the-nra-is-silent/?utm_term=.d631c566f257) killed merely for having a weapon, and implies that NRA support for gun rights applies only to white people.
1.3.4.3.1.1.2. Con: Two videos of the shooting, one by his girlfriend does not appear that she is upset by his shooting the other by the police shows the officer repeatedly telling him not to reach for his weapon before opening fire.  [www.youtube.com](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Vd7zW4aRlYE) and [www.cnn.com](https://www.cnn.com/videos/us/2017/06/22/philando-castile-facebook-and-dashcam-full-mashup-video-ctn.cnn)  I just learned that she was streaming this to facebook live which seems very odd behavior if your loved one has just been shot for what you believe is no apparent reason.
1.3.4.3.1.1.2.1. Con: Literally none of this excuses the actions of the officer.
1.3.4.3.2. Con: Police officers in general do not fear [legal gun owners](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YpTXeY6Bq7U), they are cautious because anyone they stop could potentially be a criminal and could mean them harm. That's just basic safety precautions. It's actually a non-issue so long as people [act appropriately](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=3rW5y0Vl-PY) \(as they should anyway\) when interacting with the police.
1.3.4.3.2.1. Con: [Philandro Castile](https://www.mamamia.com.au/philandro-castile/) behaved exactly as a legal gun owner is supposed to - notified police that he had a weapon in the glove box he was asked to open to get his license and registration, and that he was licensed to carry it. He was then shot and killed, essentially immediately upon doing so.
1.3.4.3.2.1.1. Con: That is contested, as it is also alleged that he continued to move after being told to stop.  If so, he did exactly the opposite of what anyone armed \(or unarmed for that matter\) is supposed to do in that situation.  Given that it takes [less than a second](https://youtu.be/fOO99qcASEM?t=4m33s) to draw and fire a gun from a car, it puts the officer in a very difficult and dangerous position and can \(and did in this case\) result in the officer making a terrible mistake.
1.3.4.3.2.1.1.1. Con: The idea that a person deserved to die, or at least that it was justified to kill them, for not immediately obeying an officer to the letter is, at best, uncomfortably close to fascism.
1.3.4.3.2.1.1.1.1. Con: That's a strawman argument.  Saying he "deserved to die" is obviously false.  If someone takes a selfie while hanging off a cliff they don't deserve to die, but they are certainly doing something unsafe that would make that more likely to happen.
1.3.4.3.2.1.1.1.2. Con: As for immediacy, before you finish reading this sentence, spot the typo and write it down.  That's about how long you have to decide and respond in positions like these if someone is about to shoot you to death or not.  Taking that into consideration, a measure of safe practices is warranted by both parties. Did he screw up?  Of course he did.  However many police officers who screwed up in the other direction have been shot and/or killed.
1.3.4.3.2.1.1.1.3. Con: Nobody has claimed that Castillo deserved to die, but that he contributed to his death by continue to move his arm where his weapon was believed to be.  If you are speeding or just driving faster than conditions allow and have a wreck that leads to your death, only truly heartless could suggest that you deserved to die but only ignorant people could claim that you did not contribute to your own death because of your choice to drive too fast.
1.3.5. Pro: Gun violence detracts from many of the obligations the government was created to adhere to, for example protection of basic rights such as the right to life. As such, the government is duty bound to take efforts to reduce that detraction.
1.3.5.1. Con: Someone misusing their own right to own a gun to murder \(deny someone else their right to life\) is already illegal. The potential for a right to be misused does not change its status as a right.
1.3.5.1.1. Con: Wrong. Translated on a global scale that would mean: each country on this planet should have the right to own atomic bombs. Totally bad idea.

The point is that the right to own a weapon, has a much lower priority than the right to not be harmed by someones \(or some country's\) weapon.
1.3.5.1.1.1. Con: This is not correct because countries that are known to be bad actors, are pressured and restricted to prevent them from developing nuclear weapons, just like known criminals are restricted from owning firearms.
1.3.6. Con: Guns did not exist for a long portion of human history, and violence/murder/war did not suddenly spring into being with the invention of guns. By all accounts, the world was far more violent before guns existed than it is now: therefore the claim that violence would disappear if a magic wand were able to get rid of all guns is unarguably false.
1.3.6.1. Con: This argument tries to reduce a gun control argument to one of violence in human nature. It does not explain the disparity in gun-related violence and death between nations with strict gun controls and the US. If the argument is that humans are fundamentally violent, this should strengthen the argument for gun control to limit the impact of violence.
1.3.6.1.1. Con: Actually quite the opposite. Despite violence being a part of human nature, so is self-preservation. The fact that guns act as an equalizer means that a 6'4 300lb man must fear a 100 pound woman if she is armed. Prior to the invention of guns, violent people could, in many situations, take what they wanted and harm who they wanted with relative impunity.
1.3.6.1.1.1. Con: Again, does not address the difference in gun violence between nations with strict gun controls and the US.
1.3.6.1.1.1.1. Con: Venezuela [banned civilian ownership](http://www.bbc.com/news/world-latin-america-18288430) of guns in 2012.  Their crime/murder rate got worse and the rate is now [between 59 and 91​ per 100,000 people](http://www.businessinsider.com/r-venezuela-says-murders-soared-to-60-per-day-in-2016-2017-3) depending on which metric you use.  The low end is over 10x the murder rate of the US, and the upper end is over 18x.  Clearly gun control is not the determining factor in the murder rate of a country.
1.3.6.1.1.2. Con: "Leveling the playing field" of violent behavior does not produce a safer society; it makes violent capability more accessible.
1.3.6.1.1.2.1. Con: The two are not mutually exclusive.  The threat of violence will often prevent violence from taking place.  Those who are not stopped by moral or ethical reasons from harming others generally refrain from doing so if they cannot commit violence with impunity.
1.3.6.1.1.2.2. Pro: Even if it were true that people were less likely to be actually assaulted, everyone would feel under constant threat of violence, and thus be paranoid and afraid at all times. That sounds like a rather miserable experience.
1.3.6.1.1.3. Con: Guns, like other weapons, largely favour the first to use them - once you've been shot, you're unlikely to be able to shoot back. As such, they favour those using them aggressively, not those using them in response to an attack.
1.3.6.1.1.3.1. Con: An armed populace helps to mitigate this problem and acts as a deterrent against violent behavior in the first place.  For example, no one tries to shoot up police stations or gun shows, not because they won't get the first shot off, but because they are surrounded by multiple people who are armed and would shoot them back if they were to make the attempt.
1.3.6.1.1.3.1.1. Con: "Armed people" are not the only reason a person would not attack a police department or a gun show. Both of those locations are more likely to have controlled entry points as well as vigilant, well-trained defenders.  Soft targets aren't just soft because they don't have guns -- it's also because they are focusing on peaceful activities such as religion, education, and entertainment and cannot grow in those areas while remaining vigilant against attackers.
1.3.6.1.1.3.1.2. Con: There have been at least two mass shootings at [Ft. Hood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fort_Hood_shooting), a literal military base.
1.3.6.1.1.3.1.2.1. Con: Only Military Police typically carry firearms therefore this argument makes no sense.
1.3.6.1.1.3.1.2.2. Pro: A military base is very similar to the world most pro-gun people envision: a few highly-trained people with guns to protect everyone else.
1.3.6.1.1.4. Con: A 100 pound woman is more likely to have any gun she has knocked out of her hand in an attack - or to be incapacitated long before she manages to draw it.
1.3.6.1.1.4.1. Con: If it is so simple to disarm someone who is armed with a gun, then there is no reason to fear armed criminals.
1.3.6.1.1.4.1.1. Con: The parent overgeneralizes the grandparent. Attackers have the ability to overwhelm and incapacitate defenders before defenders can draw a weapon for a counterattack. Therefore an armed attacker has less reason to fear an armed defender, not vice versa.
1.3.6.1.1.4.1.1.1. Con: This scenario does not change the point.  If the defender is overwhelmed either way before they have a chance to do anything, whether or not they or their attacker is armed, then it makes no difference whether the attacker is armed or not.
1.3.6.1.1.4.1.1.1.1. Con: A way to overwhelm a target is to draw your firearm first from up to 15 yards away and threaten to fire if the target moves. That makes every defense outside of a third party defender invalid. Therefore a person engaging in self defense has reason to fear an armed attacker more than an unarmed attacker, and an attacker has less reason to fear an armed defender.
1.3.6.1.1.4.1.1.2. Con: In a public setting, which does comprise some percentage of assaults, the person being attacked does not have to be the one who draws the weapon.  The 100 pound woman from the previous example could draw her weapon on a 300lb man \(or several of them\) who are attacking another civilian, and she would be able to stop the crime.  Unarmed, she would simply become another victim if she attempted to intervene.
1.3.6.1.2. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.
1.3.6.1.3. Con: Gun control does not stop violence, it only makes the transfer, purchase, and ownership of guns illegal or highly regulated. Violence itself is in the hands of individuals, not the state or legislators. No one can pass a law that says "nobody will be violent anymore."
1.3.6.2. Con: The issue here is the high fatality rate of gun violence.
1.3.6.2.1. Con: There is also a high fatality rate when people use bombs.  If people want to commit mayhem they will find a way.  Car bombs are use in other parts of the world, and there is no reason to assume that bombs or other destructive devices would not replace guns if guns were severely restricted or banned.
1.3.6.2.1.1. Con: These could all occur in any country, and yet there are not regular mass shootings in any other developed country. This implies that these are meaningful barriers to people.
1.3.6.2.1.1.1. Con: The USA is not even near the top of the list of developed countries for mass shootings. Mexico and Brazil are quite well developed. They have stricter gun measures. They have lots mass shootings. It goes with the territory of a corrupt governments and strict gun control.
1.3.6.2.1.1.1.1. Con: There is no metric of development or stability on which the US is more comparable to Brazil or Mexico than e.g. the UK or Australia.
1.3.6.2.1.1.1.1.1. Con: Anyone who has ever been to Sao Paulo can testify that it is as "developed" as any major American city. Their economy is not nearly as large as ours, but by that standard there are no other developed countries.
1.3.6.2.1.1.1.1.1.1. Con: The official [standard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developed_country) and scientific definition of developed countries would tend to disagree \(the USA doesn't even top the table\)
1.3.6.2.1.1.1.1.1.1.1. Pro: Using the same source, Mexico and Brazil are both second world in terms of "Developed" status and don't even rank in the top 50. As such, comparing the USA to them is a fallacious argument.
1.3.6.2.1.1.1.1.2. Pro: Development is more than just financial and infrastructure. It also includes trust in and quality of institutions, and how effective the government is at maintaining a monopoly on violence.
1.3.6.2.1.1.1.2. Con: The USA has the highest rate of [School shootings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/School_shooting). As for firearm related deaths, the USA comes [10th in the world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_firearm-related_death_rate), above Mexico but below Brazil. However it is the only Nation considered a "Developed" 1st world Nation in the top 10. [Brazil is not](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developed_country) considered 1st world "developed".
1.3.6.2.1.1.1.2.1. Con: If you want to protect children at schools, instead of comparing apples to oranges, there are several ways.  For instance, Utah allowed teachers, that were so inclined, to go through training and receive their concealed carry permit.  And as such, Utah has not had a school shooting in 15 years since this statute was implemented.  [sltrib.com](https://www.sltrib.com/news/2018/02/22/utah-already-allows-concealed-weapons-on-campus-could-arming-teachers-stop-shootings/)
1.3.6.2.1.1.1.2.1.1. Con: After the [Dunblane School](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dunblane_massacre) Shooting in the UK, the UK enacted stricter gun controls. There has not been a school shooting or even a fire-arm related incident in a UK school in 22 years.
1.3.6.2.1.1.2. Con: They occur in countries where guns are considerably more difficult to procure legally, like France. Shootings occur in the UK as well and [lately with greatly increased frequency even as other forms of deadly violence are also on the rise](http://www.bbc.com/news/uk-england-london-39578500), but in the UK, the victims have no chance to fight back.
1.3.6.2.1.1.3. Con: European countries also have a higher rate of [bombings](https://www.investors.com/politics/editorials/sorry-despite-gun-control-advocates-claims-u-s-isnt-the-worst-country-for-mass-shootings/).
1.3.6.3. Con: This argument confuses correlation and causation. Alleged reduction in violence cannot be attributed to the invention of guns.
1.3.6.3.1. Con: The reduction in violence is not "alleged" it's a statistical fact that is not disputed by any credible source.  Whether or not you agree with the cause, the fact that violence has gone down globally since then is undeniable
1.3.6.3.2. Con: The cause of the reduction cannot conclusively be tied solely to the invention of guns, however since the grandparent claim not only attempts to correlate the existence of guns and the safety of people in the country, with no evidence to support that speculation, this seems an appropriate response.  Either the grandparent has no basis for attempting to correlate the two, or correlation is valid, and the counter is true
1.3.6.4. Con: Exactly because violent people exist and have always existed, it makes sense to prevent people with a proven record of violence to own guns.
1.3.6.4.1. Con: People with a violent record are already prevented from purchasing or owning guns under current law. Yet somehow they still manage to get them anyways without the government or law enforcement knowing about it.
1.3.6.4.2. Con: Because a violent criminal would use a gun in an illegal way, does not mean you should remove the right to own a gun from a law abiding citizen.
1.3.6.4.2.1. Con: People are not murderous or suicidal, until they are. Those are not static traits, and can develop both over time or happen in a fit of impulsivity.
1.3.6.4.2.1.1. Con: Neither are guns, knives, rocks, or high places- until a murderous or suicidal person comes along.
1.3.6.5. Con: This argument is trying to defeat a strawman: "violence would disappear if society got rid of all guns". The argument in discussion is not about "getting rid of all guns", but restricting access to them.
1.3.6.5.1. Con: Given that "restricting access" would mean in practice that civilians would be unable to obtain/carry/use them to protect themselves this amounts to much the same thing \(ie. in Chicago, where one must show "good reason" to obtain a license, and no reason is ever considered "good"\).  Therefore it is not a strawman it is an accurate description of the results of the proposed policies.
1.3.6.6. Pro: Gun control would not and cannot regulate morality or behavior. Gun control can only punish or threaten to punish those that would violate these new laws.
1.3.7. Con: Gun control does not effectively lower the crime rate.
1.3.7.1. Pro: The occupation/hobby related gun use declaration restrictions proposed are unnecessarily onerous and unlikely to be well implemented.
1.3.7.1.1. Pro: Agencies would have to be created to manage the mapping to approved uses.
1.3.7.1.1.1. Pro: Resources would need to be spent managing the continued validity of use/possession. Security guards may get fired, quit, retire. Hunters may cease to hunt due to old age.
1.3.7.1.1.1.1. Con: There are existing frameworks for managing these issues.
1.3.7.1.1.1.1.1. Pro: Tax offices, health insurance companies and a variety of other organisations and agencies are notified by employers when someone's employment status changes.
1.3.7.1.1.1.1.2. Pro: Agencies who need to know are automatically notified about relevant deaths when death certificates are filed.
1.3.7.1.1.2. Pro: Employment/hobby-based data sets would have to be maintained and could potentially be exploited - with unexpected consequences.
1.3.7.1.1.3. Con: This could help create more jobs, which would assuage the concern that stricter gun control would mean job losses for weapons sellers and manufacturers.
1.3.7.1.1.3.1. Con: Replacing a private sector job funded by consumers with a public sector job funded by taxpayers is less desirable.
1.3.7.1.1.3.1.1. Pro: Job costs funded by consumer demand are more likely to be paid by those choosing to consume said good/service, whereas job costs funded by the government are spread across taxpayers - consumer/abstainer alike - or suffer from perils common to use taxes.
1.3.7.1.1.3.2. Pro: For jobs that may be lost from gun manufacturing, there could also be an increase in the number of regulatory and administrative positions to uphold laws.
1.3.7.1.1.4. Con: There are plenty of government departments that already deal with application processes, it's unclear why this would be particularly different or difficult to set up.
1.3.7.1.2. Pro: 58% of 125,481 Alcohol Tobacco and Firearm department's Federal Firearms Licensees \(gun dealers\) [were not inspected](https://oig.justice.gov/reports/2013/e1305.pdf) in a 5 year span \(2007-2012\). Presumably this is a far smaller and easier population to inspect than the thesis statement's population.
1.3.7.1.2.1. Con: This is a fairly straight-up enforcement failure, and one that can easily be corrected.
1.3.7.1.3. Pro: The desired effects of the declaration of use provisions could be obtained in better ways that would make such motive declarations unnecessary.
1.3.7.1.3.1. Pro: Rather than declaring my intention to hunt, we could allow anyone having passed an appropriate hunter safety course \(or grandfathered status\) eligibility to own the appropriate limited quantity of weapons deemed responsible for hunting. Their intended use is implied by their affirmative hunter training actions.
1.3.7.1.4. Con: Restrictions on hobby related guns are needed to make sure people do not amass giant gun collections.
1.3.7.1.5. Con: Setting a limit on the number of occupation/hobby related firearms should not be difficult to implement. The government will set a reasonable cap on the amount of guns people can have for a specific purpose, and people will have to abide by that law. It's as simple as setting a speed limit.
1.3.7.1.6. Pro: There is [evidence](http://www.politifact.com/wisconsin/statements/2013/feb/03/mayors-against-illegal-guns/us-files-criminal-charges-fraction-gun-denial-case/) of prosecutors not charging prohibited persons attempting to purchase firearms.
1.3.7.1.6.1. Con: -> See 1.3.7.1.2.1.
1.3.7.1.7. Pro: Gun Control also has its roots in [racial discrimination](http://www.aljazeera.com/indepth/features/2017/10/gun-control-racist-present-171006135904199.html) - keeping firearms out of the hands of blacks and other minorities.
1.3.7.1.7.1. Con: The NRA has stoked [fear of minorities](https://www.nytimes.com/2017/06/29/us/nra-ad-trump-protests.html) in order to make people scared, and thus more likely to want a gun and be against gun regulations.
1.3.7.1.7.2. Con: An astonishing number of laws have roots or links to racial discrimination - this has more to do with a history of racist law enforcement than any kind of merit assessment of the laws that were enforced in a racist way.
1.3.7.1.7.3. Pro: -> See 1.3.4.3.1.1.
1.3.7.1.7.4. Con: Unarmed people of color are shot and killed because police fear they have guns. With stricter gun control laws, police will not be as quick to assume they have guns.
1.3.7.1.8. Pro: Use provisions such as these are already implemented successfully in other countries \(eg [Australia](http://time.com/4172274/what-its-like-to-own-guns-in-a-country-with-strict-gun-control/)\)
1.3.7.1.8.1. Con: They have also been implemented successfully in Russia, which has a much higher homicide rate than the US.  The nations with the [highest homicide rates](http://www.unodc.org/documents/gsh/data/GSH2013_Homicide_count_and_rate.xlsx) tend to have [very restrictive gun laws](http://www.gunpolicy.org).
1.3.7.1.8.1.1. Con: It is likely that the gun laws were implemented as a response to street violence \(e.g. Brazil or Mexico\), so that the police could more effectively combat the violence.
1.3.7.1.8.1.1.1. Pro: Making guns illegal allows law enforcement to intervene in organized crime activities, as well as seize their weapons.
1.3.7.1.8.1.1.1.1. Con: This is not true, historically. Government prohibitions tend to encourage organized crime as they become the only sellers of banned items. See: Alcohol, Drugs, Automatic weapons.
1.3.7.1.8.1.1.2. Pro: The existing violence means that their murder rates pre-gun control were significantly higher than the US's now. The decrease in murder rate is what is important, not the total.
1.3.7.1.8.1.1.3. Con: This may well be the case, but it doesn't make it a strong argument for gun control. Mexico's current gun control statutes appear to go back to 1972. Their most violent year \(that with the highest rate of homicides\)? 2017. With the population effectively disarmed, the police routinely use executions to maintain control. There's no good news for Americans wishing to make the USA more like Mexico.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2. Con: [Studies](https://www.nytimes.com/2017/11/07/world/americas/mass-shootings-us-international.html) have demonstrated that gun violence and mass shootings are significantly linked to per capita gun ownership.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1. Pro: More guns in circulation means more gun-related deaths.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1. Pro: The US's rate of gun deaths is problematically high.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.1. Pro: On an average day, 96 Americans are killed by with guns.[everytownresearch.org](https://everytownresearch.org/gun-violence-by-the-numbers/)
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.2. Pro: In the US, guns were the [leading cause](http://www.bbc.com/news/world-us-canada-34996604) of death by homicide \(66.6% of all homicides\) and by suicide \(52.2% of all suicides\).
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.3. Pro: The scale of mass shootings has been increasing at an [alarming rate](https://www.theguardian.com/us-news/datablog/2017/nov/06/not-your-imagination-mass-shootings-now-happen-more-frequently-in-the-us).  Some form of sensible legislative action must be done.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.4. Pro: In 2013, more than [500 people](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gun_violence_in_the_United_States) in America died from accidental discharge of a firearm.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.4.1. Con: Proper gun education and better maintenance on guns would reduce this problem. In other words, this is a user error.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.4.1.1. Con: This education and maintenance doesn't exist under the status quo where guns are legal and accepted. It is unclear why this is likely to change.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.4.1.1.1. Con: That's not really true. While knowledge may vary most gun owners understand the basic safety rules of firearm ownership \(treat all guns as if they are loaded, never point a gun at something you don't want to shoot, finger off the trigger until you are ready to fire, be aware of what is around and behind your target\). Post a picture or video of you breaking any one of these rules on a pro-gun facebook page for example and you'll immediately be called out on it.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.4.1.2. Con: When user error is easy to commit and has deadly consequences, it is appropriate to put in place more substantial protections than mere education.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.4.1.3. Con: While this is surely user error, the best way to avoid this problem is to remove the source, which is guns.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.4.2. Con: Rather than greater controls on weapons, a greater emphasis on gun safety should be lauded.  Additionally, stricter laws regarding accountability and levels of consequence should be put in place for gun owners who do not safeguard their weapons from children.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.4.3. Con: The death toll for accidental firearm discharges in the US is [less than 500 per year](https://www.cdc.gov/nchs/data/nvsr/nvsr65/nvsr65_04.pdf), in a country of 312 million people with approximately 100 million gun owners. That translates to a 0.00016% chance \(per year\) of being killed from an accidental discharge.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.4.4. Con: That constitutes negligence on some level, which may already be criminal. Until the point at which the law is broken, all owners should be innocent until proven guilty. If gun related deaths are the problem here, and we're insistent on prosecuting, the channel to do such is through negligence, not to criminalize the ownership of guns.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5. Pro: Possession of a firearm makes a person significantly more likely to [commit suicide](https://www.cbsnews.com/news/study-guns-in-home-increase-suicide-homicide-risk/).
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.1. Pro: [Half](https://afsp.org/about-suicide/suicide-statistics/) of all suicides in the US are done using a gun. There is [clear sociological evidence](https://www.hsph.harvard.edu/hicrc/firearms-research/gun-ownership-and-use/) that the ease of killing oneself is enough to persuade one to turn depression into suicide. This is also reflected in the numbers. So you have evidence both in the numbers and by psychological and sociological experts saying the same thing.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.1.1. Con: All of those things are not only absurdly costly \(annual checks on 100 million people, in order to find 20,000 \(0.02%\), would not be feasible, and would have dubious efficacy even within that small percentage.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.1.1.1. Con: Given the broader policy is designed to result in a significant reduction in gun ownership, this is a rather overestimate of the likely costs.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.1.1.1.1. Con: Why is it acceptable to punish law abiding citizens, simply because you do not like the things that they enjoy?
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.1.1.2. Con: You can fund costly projects through the taxation of the items in question. And something possibly not being effective isn't a good reason not to try it when lives are on the line, doing something to solve the problem is clearly better than doing nothing.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.1.1.2.1. Con: -> See 1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.1.1.1.1.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.1.2. Con: If guns were the issue, Japan, which has pretty much banned guns altogether would have a lower suicide rate than the US instead of [one of the highest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suicide_in_Japan).
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.1.2.1. Con: *If guns were the ONLY issue.* Just because Japan has higher rates of suicide, does not mean that guns do not contribute to suicides in the US.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.2. Con: A desperately suicidal person will simply find other means. Rather than focusing on gun issues, we should increase mental health monitoring, services and suicide prevention.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.2.1. Con: There is no reason we can't simultaneously try and resolve the factors that lead to suicide at the same time as removing the method they use to do it.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.2.2. Con: Suicide-by-gun is a particularly instantaneous form of suicide, giving those with access to it very little time to reconsider or seek medical help.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.2.3. Con: Guns are, by far, the easiest and quickest method of suicide with the lowest chance of intervention between the act and the actual death.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.2.4. Pro: People will just find other ways. Japan, for example, has a [very high suicide rate](https://www.tofugu.com/japan/suicide-in-japan/) and perhaps the strictest gun control regime in the world.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.3. Pro: Having access to a quick, easy method of death is particularly dangerous in the context of suicide, because suicide is often done at a person's worst possible moment, and thus is rarely repeated if failed. Suicide by gun has a 90% success rate, while suicide by other method is below [10%](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=lgD9AlxZxNE).
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.3.1. Pro: -> See 1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.2.2.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.3.2. Con: There is no guarantee that someone who passes the licensing/mental health tests will not use their gun for a suicide attempt.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.3.2.1. Con: If they pass the mental health test it is less likely that they would use the gun for suicide.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.3.3. Pro: People, especially teenagers, suffering from depression and with suicidal tendencies wouldn't have easy access to something that could help them end their lives.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.4. Con: This is a misunderstanding of the findings of the study. The findings are that there exists a correlation between firearms ownership and suicide tendency, not that owning a firearm literally compels a person to suicide. If anything, this study should imply that more research should be done on why there appears to be a population of people with latent suicide tendencies only held back by a lack of impulsive options.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.5. Pro: Self-inflicted gunshot wounds are more likely to be fatal than other methods.

1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.6. Con: The government should not regulate how much a person can hurt themselves.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.6.1. Pro: If a person wants to commit suicide, then that should be their prerogative.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.6.1.1. Con: This type of nihilism would generally be abhorred in most public policy discussions \(for instance in the discussion of drug abuse, automobile laws, and in safety more generally\). It shouldn't be tolerated in gun laws.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.6.1.2. Con: Those who attempt suicide often do not do so in a considered, rational manner, but due to a short-term crisis, or mental health issue.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.1.5.6.2. Con: This is a reason to legalise assisted suicide, something that can be carried out with proper checks and balances to ensure that someone is not likely to change their mind. Guns are a poor substitute for that.

1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.4. Pro: Gun control laws in CA [have demonstrated strong correlations in preventing accidental gun deaths due to law abiding gun owners acting in more safe ways with firearms.](http://lawcenter.giffords.org/gun-laws/state-law/california/)
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.4.1. Con: Some modifications made to firearms to make them compliant with CA law actually make them less safe.  The range by me will not allow some of these mods on the range as they are CA compliant, but now require a gunsmith to disassemble the firearm with a live round in it if there is a jam.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.4.2. Con: Gun related accidents have been [dropping](http://lawcenter.giffords.org/gun-deaths-and-injuries-statistics/) in recent years.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.5. Pro: Forbidding the use of guns [drastically lowers](https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2012/07/a-land-without-guns-how-japan-has-virtually-eliminated-shooting-deaths/260189/) the death rate of their citizens.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.6. Con: The number of guns in circulation does not determine how many of those guns will be used to kill.

1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.8.1. Pro: True if you are a murderous or suicidal person. But then this is also true of poison, knives, rocks, high places..
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.8.1.1. Con: Very few people \(even criminals\) are motivated to kill others. Sometimes gun deaths occur accidentally, or in a rage fit, or when a criminal faces a victim armed with a gun. Banning guns will greatly reduce the number of lethal outcomes.

1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.8.1.3. Con: One study looking at [uses of guns kept at home](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/m/pubmed/9715182/) found that for every time one was used in self-defence, there were four accidental shootings, seven assaults or homicides, and 11 attempted or completed suicides.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.8.1.3.1. Con: Firearms ownership is not a random event. [Some may own firearms specifically because they are likely to be victimized.](https://www.nap.edu/catalog/10881/firearms-and-violence-a-critical-review)
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.8.1.3.2. Con: Comparing the number of times a gun is used defensively by a law abiding citizen to stop crime to the total number of crimes is dishonest. People who are carrying are generally unlikely to be victimized in the first place, and your analysis also implies that the guns themselves were responsible for those crimes which is patently untrue.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.8.1.3.2.1. Con: This seems to assume that criminals have perfect knowledge of whether someone is armed, which is simply not true.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.8.1.3.2.2. Con: Gun owners are more likely to have been [victims of crime](http://news.gallup.com/poll/199235/crime-victims-likely-own-guns.aspx) in the last 12 months than non-gun owners. This holds true even when controlling for whether someone fears crime \(in order to determine whether they might have just bought the gun after the crime, which on the data seems unlikely\). The data does not support the idea that owning a gun has a sufficient impact on whether you are a victim of crime such that data about what else is likely to happen with your gun is skewed.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.8.1.3.2.2.1. Con: Your poll states, "Although it is not possible to know from the survey questions whether the crime prompted the individual to buy a gun or if the person owned a gun before the crime occurred" therefore your statement that it is unlikely that someone bought a gun after being victimized is impossible to support.

1.3.7.1.8.1.2.2. Con: "Gun Violence", but not Violence. Countries with the highest homicide rates in the world tend to have very restrictive gun laws. Mass shootings do correlate with gun ownership, but they are also outliers and the vast majority of them happen in places with very strict bans on firearms, which is to say, mass shooters seek out places where they have the only gun. There's never been one at a gun show and it's hard to imagine a higher "per capita gun ownership" than in the hall at a gun show.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.2.1. Con: -> See 1.3.6.1.1.3.1.2.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.2.2. Pro: When I say mass shootings are outliers, I mean in the US. They account for less than 2 tenths of a percent of homicides. In Finland, where they have quite strict gun control, in 2007 and 2008, mass shootings accounted for nearly 8% of all homicides.  You can slice and dice the numbers as you like, but while mass shootings are too common and big news, the vast majority of gun violence here is gang related and is also concentrated in municipalities with restrictive gun regulations.
1.3.7.1.8.1.2.2.3. Con: This argument brings up the point that there is a need for gun control at a federal level, not just at a local level. A shooter may choose a place with restrictive gun laws in order to commit their attack, but they have the ability to procure their firearms from places with far fewer restrictions on gun ownership, e.g. a gun show. Restrictions on a federal level would help ensure that shooters cannot easily bring a weapon into a state with more restrictive legislation.
1.3.7.1.8.2. Pro: Gun related crime is rare in Australia.
1.3.7.1.8.2.1. Con: We are using statistic from a country with a population of only 23 million and comparing to the U.S. with a population of well over 300 million.  You cant do that. Compare apples to apples: Australia's 233 gun deaths look mighty bad compared to their small population. Our 11,000 is about the same if you look at population.
1.3.7.1.8.2.1.1. Con: I can't support this. The math is way off.  We have 15X the population and 55X the homicide rate.

1.3.7.1.8.2.3. Con: The pro-gun argument is that guns allow people to defend themselves from all kinds of criminals, regardless of whether or not the criminals use a gun.  "Gun-related" crime is rare, but overall crime is actually worse than in Australia.  They have [twice the burglary rate](http://www.nationmaster.com/country-info/stats/Crime/Burglaries), a higher [per-capita rape rate](http://www.nationmaster.com/country-info/stats/Crime/Violent-crime/Rapes-per-million-people), a significantly [higher rate of kidnapping](http://www.nationmaster.com/country-info/stats/Crime/Kidnappings), and they are [number 1 \(next to new zealand\)](http://www.nationmaster.com/country-info/stats/Crime/Property-crime-victims) in the percentage of the population who is victims of property crimes.
1.3.7.1.8.2.3.1. Con: There are plenty of other methods for preventing these crimes which are not nearly as dangerous for the victim or Bystanders, including home alarm systems, tazers, and self-defense knowledge.
1.3.7.1.8.2.4. Con: The US homicide rate fell as much or more than Australia's in percentile terms over the same period. Linking the decrease in homicide to gun control directly is difficult.

1.3.7.2. Pro: The policy fails to address the root of the issue with gun violence in the US which is cultural.
1.3.7.2.1. Pro: The U.S. as a whole is not a homogeneous society. This suggests that culture is more to blame for high crime rates than firearm ownership.
1.3.7.2.1.1. Con: Rather, this demonstrates that the US does not have uniform gun control laws, and that a variety of other factors - wealth disparity, poverty, education rates, population density, etc - also have an impact on crime rates.
1.3.7.2.2. Con: It is far more difficult to regulate culture than gun possession. Seeing as how both are required for gun violence, focus should be placed on the easiest condition to impact.
1.3.7.2.2.1. Con: This argument assumes that laws can trump culture. They cannot; culture is more powerful. If the U.S. instituted an Australian-style gun ban/buyback, it's unlikely that Americans would comply in turning in their weapons.
1.3.7.2.2.1.1. Con: History has shown that laws as an incentive mechanism can have an effect on cultural values.

1.3.7.2.2.1.2.1.2. Con: The then-Deputy Prime Minister was [literally burnt in effigy](http://www.smh.com.au/comment/how-australia-beat-the-gun-lobby-and-passed-gun-control-20171003-gytvn4.html) at rallies against the laws he was shepherding through.

"about 1 million firearms in New York State meet the law’s assault-weapon criteria, but just 44,000 have been registered".
