1.3.7.3.5.1.1. Con: The definition varies, but eliminating for domestic violence and gang activity shows that the types of mass shootings that lead to the public outcry of late [are not](https://www.politico.com/magazine/story/2017/10/04/mass-shootings-more-deadly-frequent-research-215678) more common over the past 5 years.
1.3.7.3.5.1.1.1. Con: They are also, per the same source, significantly more deadly, coinciding with increasing availability of more deadly firearms.
1.3.7.3.5.1.1.2. Con: There's not a particular reason to exclude domestic violence or gang activity when considering whether we should be concerned about the rate of shooting fatalities. These shootings also have victims, whom we should care about.
1.3.7.3.5.1.2. Con: [37% of households](http://www.people-press.org/2013/03/12/section-3-gun-ownership-trends-and-demographics/#profile-guns) have a gun. Let's say that's about 100 million people. So this example means that 0.0015% are, indeed, not law-abiding citizens. This is an extremely small percentage.
1.3.7.3.5.1.2.1. Con: This is a poor comparison. Firearm violence has [varied between 400,000 and 1.5 million incidents a year](https://www.bjs.gov/content/pub/pdf/fv9311.pdf) in the last 30 years or so - to compare only to the most extreme cases is misleading.
1.3.7.3.5.1.2.1.1. Pro: In addition, not all gun owners who commit crimes with their guns will commit crimes with their guns every year.
1.3.7.3.5.2. Con: Those gun owners that love democracy, also understand it. Constitutional law supersedes federal and state law. If Congress passes a law that is clearly unconstitutional, instead of following the amendment process, they are subverting democracy, and gun owners are unlikely to comply. Look at "Assault weapon" bans in Connecticut and New York requiring existing owners to register and/or get rid of their rifles if they have plastic handles, which resulted in massive civil disobedience.
1.3.7.3.5.2.1. Con: Even if they considered the law to be unconstitutional \(it does not become legally so until challenged\) they would be bound to follow it, until they challenged its constitutionality in court. Civil disobedience or any other type of law breaking would be unethical for gun-owners because they love their country.
1.3.7.3.5.2.1.1. Con: To say that "gun owners love their country" may be a vast oversimplification, at least in some cases. It could be more accurate to say that many gun owners love the ideals and philosophies which their country represents, stands for, or used to stand for.
1.3.7.3.5.2.1.2. Con: Civil disobedience is exactly how laws often get [challenged](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scopes_Trial). Someone who is arrested under an unjust/unconstitutional law will appeal to higher courts and the law will get overturned when they are declared unconstitutional.
1.3.7.3.5.2.1.3. Con: On laws that clearly violate the constitution, civil disobedience would not be unethical precisely because gun-owners love their country. Consider this: If there was a law passed that said Islam was now illegal, and it was also illegal to refuse to report known Muslims to the authorities, would you consider it unethical for patriotic Americans/Muslims to refuse to report others or to give up their religion? No, of course not, the law would be ignored until it was struck down by the court.
1.3.7.3.6. Pro: -> See 1.3.1.1.1.
1.3.7.3.7. Pro: There are roughly [1000 extreme](https://www.splcenter.org/active-antigovernment-groups-united-states) anti-government groups in the US, and many of those consider gun rights to be paramount.
1.3.7.3.7.1. Con: That’s a reason to enact gun restrictions. Right wing terrorism is getting out of hand in the US with the [recent plane bombing attempt](https://www.citizen-times.com/story/news/local/2017/10/10/bomb-airport-ammonium-nitrate-fuel-oil-mix-suspect-make-first-appearance/749394001/), and there needs to be appropriate measures in place to restrain access to weaponry.
1.3.7.3.7.2. Pro: The list cited does not include only violent anti-government groups, many of those in these groups are currently law-abiding, but willing to turn on the government in cases they see as overreach.
1.3.7.3.7.3. Con: The US should not create its laws around the desires of extremist groups.
1.3.7.3.7.4. Con: It would be optically harmful for extremist groups that support gun rights to commit acts of violence using guns, so they probably wouldn't respond in that manner.
1.3.7.3.8. Pro: Strict gun laws would likely be enforced more harshly against minority communities.
1.3.7.3.8.1. Pro: African-American men are [2.8 times more likely](http://ajph.aphapublications.org/doi/full/10.2105/AJPH.2016.303575#_i3) to be killed by police than white men.
1.3.7.3.8.2. Pro: Black people are disproportionally killed by police officers, while white people can attempt to [violently seize federal](http://thehill.com/homenews/news/347611-cliven-bundy-followers-found-not-guilty-in-armed-standoff-case) land and be captured alive.
1.3.7.3.8.2.1. Con: Actually it is a common misconception that black people are disproportionately killed by police officers. The stats were reviewed and found [no racial bias](http://www.washingtontimes.com/news/2016/jul/11/no-racial-bias-police-shootings-study-harvard-prof/) in lethal use of force in any given police interaction. In fact, if the police officer was white there was sometimes a slight bias against using lethal force on a black suspect.
1.3.7.3.8.2.1.1. Con: This study has been criticised, and is certainly not believable on its own. A followup investigation found that in fact black males are [2.8 times](http://ajph.aphapublications.org/doi/full/10.2105/AJPH.2016.303575#_i3) more likely to be killed by police than whites.
1.3.7.3.8.2.1.1.1. Pro: Importantly, this follow-up study accounts for the significantly higher rate of police encounters that African-American people experience. Failing to account for this risks hiding one impact of racist policing \(disproportionate use of lethal force\) behind a different impact of racist policing \(disproportionate rates of police initiating encounters\).
1.3.7.3.8.2.1.1.1.1. Con: Disproportionate rates of police initiating encounters with a certain race does not prove racist policing unless there is evidence that race is the primary factor for initiating the encounter.  Without that evidence, it simply indicates that there are more encounters.  For example, if the police are in a high crime area that is predominantly populated by black people, they are going to have disproportionately larger numbers of encounters with black suspects.
1.3.7.3.8.2.1.1.1.1.1. Pro: This is equally true of Hispanic and White neighborhoods
1.3.7.3.8.2.1.1.2. Con: This study has the same failure in methodology that was corrected for in the original study: the deaths were measured against the total population of each demographic, instead of the number of instances of police interaction. Percentage-wise, more black people had interactions with police for suspected crimes, however the rate at which those interactions turned lethal still shows no bias from the police.
1.3.7.3.8.3. Pro: The licensing process can be [discriminatory](http://www.washingtontimes.com/news/2014/sep/29/chicago-concealed-carry-gun-permit-law-disarms-poo/) towards minority groups. In Illinois, only eight percent of African Americans have been able to secure licenses.
1.3.7.3.8.4. Con: This happens in the status quo because gun laws are not universalized across states and can be bent to exclude people.
1.3.7.3.8.5. Con: This already happens anyway, so changes in the law won't matter.
1.3.7.3.8.6. Pro: Historically gun control was instituted to harm minorities; although a majority of Americans clearly supported these measures, they fundamentally eroded the principles America is built on.
1.3.7.3.8.6.1. Pro: President Reagan enacted gun control as a [response](https://www.huffingtonpost.com/entry/black-panthers-california-1967_us_568accfce4b014efe0db2f40) to the Black Panthers.
1.3.7.3.8.6.2. Pro: Some California sheriffs [stated](http://www.sacbee.com/news/state/california/article158150224.html) their departments could or would use the law against high capacity magazines to add charges to the rap sheets of gang members, which could affect racial minorities at higher rates due to a systemic racial bias attached to anti-gang operations within US law enforcement.
1.3.7.3.8.6.2.1. Pro: An [in-depth study](https://repository.law.umich.edu/cgi/viewcontent.cgi?referer=https://www.google.com/&httpsredir=1&article=1025&context=mjrl) of the application of the RICO Act showed that the vast majority of prosecutions target gangs that are affiliated with racial minorities, while similar White-affiliated groups are often not labeled as "gangs" by the government and are therefore not targeted by law enforcement.
1.3.7.3.8.6.3. Pro: -> See 1.3.4.3.1.1.
1.3.7.3.8.6.4. Con: The end being wrong does not make the means wrong.
1.3.7.3.9. Con: No one would consider retreating from enacting a law restricting or opposing terrorist groups because it might result in a terrorist response. Nor should they consider the response of gun owners that refuse to follow the law.
1.3.7.3.9.1. Con: Untrue. A law requiring fingerprinting and occasional house searches for those who attend mosques deemed radical would be described by proponents as opposing terrorist groups. But some would correctly argue that such heavy-handed policy increases the risk of terrorism. By removing rights from innocent gun owners to target criminal ones, you risk making more criminals than you started with.
1.3.7.3.9.2. Con: Then maybe we should consider outlawing ownership of firearms and other things that can be used as weapons by African Americans because they make up 13% of the population but commit [52%](https://www.channel4.com/news/factcheck/factcheck-black-americans-commit-crime) of the homicides.  The problem with this argument is that it would infringe on law abiding Black citizens.
1.3.7.3.9.3. Con: Gun owners are not terrorists who simply want to kill/hurt people to produce fear. They would be reacting specifically to a direct threat to the fundamental values and laws upon which the country was built.
1.3.7.3.10. Pro: The NRA is immensely powerful and would likely orchestrate protests and backlash against this policy.
1.3.7.3.10.1. Con: Violent protest and backlash would simply demonstrate the need for regulations and lead to stricter measures down the line. Gun proponents' main argument is that they are law-abiding citizens.
1.3.7.3.10.2. Con: Protests and backlash do not always mean violence.
1.3.7.3.10.3. Pro: The NRA is so powerful that it was able to get Congress to pass a bill that[prevents the CDC](http://www.latimes.com/business/hiltzik/la-fi-hiltzik-gun-research-funding-20160614-snap-story.html) from using gun violence statistics to "advocate for gun control," which effectively prohibits them from doing any kind of meaningful research into gun violence, and the ATF from using computers.
1.3.7.3.10.3.1. Con: If a research group is advocating for a specific policy, then their research is going to be biased to support that advocacy.  Requiring that the CDC remain objective is not a bad thing.
1.3.7.3.10.3.2. Pro: The original author of that law, [Jay Dickey](https://www.cnn.com/2015/12/02/politics/jay-dickey-gun-violence-research/), now argues that the CDC must be allowed to research gun violence.
1.3.7.3.10.3.2.1. Pro: Researching gun violence is not the same as advocating for gun control.  Researching means determining why and possibly where gun violence occurs, including accidental gun shootings.  If it is determined that certain chemicals occur in the drinking water where the most violence occurs or that most people who commit violence have a history of concussions then we would need to determine how to reduce these causes.
1.3.7.3.10.3.3. Con: Requiring the CDC to remain neutral is a good thing, because otherwise they could promote policies that hinder research for AIDS or other diseases because AIDS disproportionately affects homosexual males and promiscuous individuals.  If the CDC  were run by people who believe that either of these is wrong, they could advocate for letting these 'sinners' or relative minorities die.
1.3.7.3.10.3.4. Pro: Reversing Citizen's United v FEC ruling and limiting amounts spent on campaigns would solve NRA \(and other special interest group\) control of legislators in US allowing common sense governance.
1.3.7.3.10.4. Con: If they were to orchestrate any violent protests they would be breaking the law, and would likely be punished severely.
1.3.7.4. Con: Other forms of licensing have proven to be effective. Gun control could work in the same way.
1.3.7.4.1. Pro: Age requirements for licensing have been successfully used for a number of things including for cars, alcohol and tobacco.
1.3.7.4.1.1. Con: Age restrictions are always a proxy for some other qualification \(height, maturity, etc\). Given that these qualifications can be met at any age, all age restrictions are inherently arbitrary. This means that many qualified people are cut out from whatever the restriction bans for no reason.
1.3.7.4.1.2. Con: Being a minor is not inherently reason to prevent the owning or operation of a firearm.
1.3.7.4.1.2.1. Con: If we don’t allow minors to drink, drive or make decisions about their health, it doesn’t seem unreasonable to deny them access to a weapon that can easily kill.
1.3.7.4.1.2.2. Con: Minors have more trouble conceptualizing and internalizing the consequences of their actions than adults. They also tend to be incredibly impulsive. Because these traits are inherent to minors, they should be restricted from gun ownership.
1.3.7.4.1.3. Pro: Furthermore, alcohol is highly regulated because of the potential dangers it poses. There is a minimum age of purchase, liability legislation \(i.e. a bartender in Colorado can be held responsible if they serve someone who later ends up injured from drunk driving\) and there are taxes that increase the price to deter heavy consumption.
1.3.7.4.2. Pro: Limiting access to drivers that have met minimum standards works to keep dangerous people off the road.
1.3.7.4.2.1. Con: Purchasing and using a firearm already has higher standards than similar actions with a vehicle. These high standards do not prevent events like the shooting at Sandy Hook, therefore strengthening regulations will not change firearm violence.
1.3.7.4.2.2. Pro: Similarly, if people are caught using their firearms dangerously, they can have their access to those firearms taken away.
1.3.7.4.3. Pro: With licensing, stolen goods can easily be returned to their owners \(as is the case with cars\).
1.3.7.4.3.1. Con: The ease with which vehicles are identified is a characteristic of vehicles, not registration. It is [far more difficult](https://www.scientificamerican.com/article/how-can-a-bullet-be-trace/) to identify a specific gun by its bullet wound than a specific car by its collision.
1.3.7.4.3.2. Con: I don't believe a victim of a stolen car would tell you how "easy" it was to receive their vehicle back to them. Some never see their vehicle again. Licensing didn't prevent this.
1.3.7.4.4. Con: Responsible people should not have privileges \(or rights\) taken away because of irresponsible people.
1.3.7.4.4.1. Con: Sacrificing individual liberties for the sake of shared protections is the defining characteristic of the social compact from which government is derived.
1.3.7.4.4.2. Con: It's a lot more challenging and costly to own and operate a vehicle. Requiring safety features, speed limits and insurance probably came about from the actions of irresponsible people.
1.3.7.4.4.3. Con: People's privileges should end at the point at which other people are put in danger.
1.3.7.4.5. Con: -> See 1.3.1.1.1.
1.3.7.4.6. Pro: Just because we cannot legislate all gun violence away does not mean that we shouldn't make attempts to prevent at least some of the violence. We can't stop all crazy/drunk people from getting behind the wheel, yet we still have road laws, seatbelt laws, age restrictions, required license, etc.
1.3.7.4.6.1. Pro: Despite our best efforts to get it right the first time, many laws require tweaking post passage. Perfection should not be the enemy of good when it comes to lawmaking.
1.3.7.4.6.2. Con: And we probably have more laws than that regulating firearms. There are literally thousands on the books at the federal, state, and even local levels. The point is not that there should be no regulation, the point is that there is already a reasonable amount of regulation, which in fact goes too far in some places, which has a negative effect. In some places you are required to not only have a permit but must show "good reason", \(however virtually all reasons are then denied\).
1.3.7.4.6.2.1. Con: If the argument is that there is already too much regulation we can remove other regulation as we implement this.
1.3.7.4.6.2.2. Con: Regulation without control mechanisms isn't effective by itself. [For example police officers in California said they were using regulations only to fill the rap sheet of "gang members" and were going to leave the general public alone](http://www.sacbee.com/news/state/california/article158150224.html). This shows that regulation needs clear enforcement mechanisms or it's likely to be abused by law enforcement to hurt marginalized communities.
1.3.7.4.7. Con: There is no clear proof that other forms of licensing have proven effective.
1.3.7.4.7.1. Con: Top graduated driver licensing requirements reduce 16 year old fatal crashes by 20%. [John Hopkins School of Medicine](https://www.jhsph.edu/news/news-releases/2006/baker-gdl.html)
1.3.7.4.8. Con: Guns sold on the black market are likely to give higher profits to criminals, gangs, cartels, and the mafia which traffic these products.
1.3.7.4.8.1. Con: That may be true, but it doesn't directly support the claim. A richer criminal isn't necessarily worse than a poor criminal.
1.3.7.4.8.2. Con: Gun trafficking rings are unlikely to only be trafficking guns - they have plenty of other criminal activity to make profits off in the absence of a market for illegal firearms.
1.3.7.4.8.3. Con: Claiming that black market guns generate a high profit for criminals without evidence as to why they do is a red herring. It could be because they charge high prices or because they steal the guns and therefore get them for free but without knowing whether it is one of these or both, there is no way to address the actual issue.
1.3.7.4.9. Con: This argument has the same flaw as the argument for banning alcohol \(illuminated by the disaster of prohibition\) - driving things underground makes them more not less dangerous.
1.3.7.4.9.1. Con: The difference is that prohibition 'prohibited' alcohol entirely, rather than licensing and controlling it. Consider cigarettes - they are heavily restricted and taxed in many countries, and smoking rates have dropped precipitously, but its still more common to buy them at a local store than on the black market. The proposal does not suggest 'prohibition' of guns, just restrictions to important and appropriate uses by responsible owners.
1.3.7.4.9.2. Con: Unlike alcohol, gun manufacturing requires fairly advanced machinery. As a result, it is significantly harder to maintain an underground market in guns than in alcohol.
1.3.7.4.9.2.1. Con: [Two pieces of pipe, a nail and a shell are enough to make a gun](https://s14-eu5.ixquick.com/cgi-bin/serveimage?url=http:%2F%2F1y7vgdz53a11xyb91s53s6d6.wpengine.netdna-cdn.com%2Fwp-content%2Fuploads%2F2016%2F06%2Fshotgun-6-1024x320.jpg&sp=6daf1d7258e1582aa4e54dc952024d0c).
1.3.7.4.9.2.1.1. Con: In the literal sense, yes, but not an effective one.
1.3.7.4.10. Pro: Additionally gun licenses could generate incremental revenue to offset the unintended consequences of guns \(injury / health costs\).
1.3.7.4.11. Con: In [Jamaica](https://crimeresearch.org/2013/12/murder-and-homicide-rates-before-and-after-gun-bans/), the homicide rate rose substantially after the implementation of gun control [\[link to chart\]](http://progun.ph/sites/default/files/jamaica-murder-rate-1970-2000.jpg)
1.3.7.4.11.1. Con: -> See 1.3.7.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.
1.3.7.4.12. Pro: A proper licensing process could reduce gun-related crimes of passion.
1.3.7.4.12.1. Pro: Requiring people to apply for license would prevent people from impulsively buying a gun in a fit of anger.
1.3.7.4.13. Con: Gun licensing already exists.
1.3.7.5. Con: The evidence suggests that the rate of gun ownership in a community [correlates with a higher rate of crime](https://www.scientificamerican.com/article/more-guns-do-not-stop-more-crimes-evidence-shows/).
1.3.7.5.1. Con: Correlation is not causation. Living in higher crime areas prompts more people to want firearms for protection.
1.3.7.5.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.3.7.1.8.1.2.1.8.1.3.1.
1.3.7.5.1.2. Con: The studies cited largely control for this, through a variety of methodological means.
1.3.7.5.1.2.1. Pro: For example, controlling for other variables that make crime more likely, like the urban/rural divide.
1.3.7.5.1.2.2. Pro: For example, looking at states that tightened or loosened gun control laws before and after that change, and comparing their crime rates to crime rates in otherwise similar states.
1.3.7.5.2. Con: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.2.
1.3.7.5.3. Con: The studies \([here's another more recent, more rigorous one](https://afsp.org/about-suicide/suicide-statistics/)\) have no way to determine gun ownership. They all use the same proxy - suicide by firearm, but they do not control for race/gender. Women are much less likely to perpetrate violent crime, but commit about a third of suicides \(rarely using guns\). African-American males are disproportionately convicted of violent crimes but suicide rates are 1/3 that of non-Hispanic whites. None appear to indicate if the trend survives demographic splits.
1.3.7.6. Con: -> See 1.3.6.2.
1.3.7.7. Pro: -> See 1.3.7.4.11.
1.3.7.8. Pro: -> See 1.3.7.2.5.2.2.2.
1.3.7.9. Con: -> See 1.3.7.2.6.3.
1.3.7.10. Con: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.4.
1.3.7.11. Con: Connecticut added very strict gun laws. Since then, gun crimes have gone down by up to [50%](https://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/govbeat/wp/2015/06/12/gun-killings-fell-by-40-percent-after-connecticut-passed-this-law/?utm_term=.7fb9184d0f30).
1.3.7.11.1. Con: California, by contrast, has introduced various gun control laws, [but has not seen a decrease in firearm popularity as a weapon in assaults and murder.](https://openjustice.doj.ca.gov/2016/homicide) At a national level, this is also the case, indicating that Connecticut is an invalid anecdotal example.
1.3.7.11.1.1. Con: -> See 1.3.7.2.5.1.1.1.
1.3.7.11.1.2. Con: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.4.
1.3.7.11.2. Con: Gun crimes and gun deaths cannot be equivocated. This is because deaths factor in accidents and justified shootings that result in deaths. Crimes include assaults and murder, as well as brandishing the weapon and illegal possession.
1.3.7.12. Con: Japan has made it 99.9% illegal to own a gun and [they have](https://www.cbsnews.com/news/how-u-s-gun-deaths-compare-to-other-countries/) almost 0 deaths from guns, and 17 times less homicide overall.
1.3.7.12.1. Con: Japanese Americans have similarly low rates of violent crime, which indicates that it is culture, not access to firearms, that drives gun violence.
1.3.7.13. Pro: Stricter gun control laws probably won't decrease the number of guns in circulation and might even increase the number of illegal guns in circulation, which creates a bigger problem. During the Prohibition Era, when alcohol was illegal, Al Capone and other bootleggers got rich off of people desperate for alcohol. If we allow stricter gun laws to be passed, then we are giving criminals more opportunities to gain revenue.
1.3.7.14. Pro: Numerous studies in the US have shown that the higher the rate of firearm ownership is, the lower the violent crime rate is.
1.3.7.14.1. Con: The evidence for this is at best [mixed](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pubmed/26091930).
1.3.7.14.2. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.1.1.2.3.2.2.1.3.1.6.
1.3.7.14.3. Pro: Despite more firearms being present, the overall rate of firearms violence is actually lower than at the height of gun control regulations.[factcheck.org](https://www.factcheck.org/2012/12/gun-rhetoric-vs-gun-facts/)
1.3.7.14.4. Pro: We assume there is a greater problem with gun violence and mass shootings in the US, but this is not the case.

You would assume that with 1/3 more people  [\(around 100 million\)](http://www.multpl.com/united-states-population/table) in the US since the 1980 and with [gun ownership percentages remaining the same](https://www.statista.com/statistics/249740/percentage-of-households-in-the-united-states-owning-a-firearm/) \( with now 40 million more homes owning guns\) that the number of gun violence would increase proportionally. 

[However gun violence was down around 49% from 1993 to 2014](http://www.pewsocialtrends.org/2013/05/07/gun-homicide-rate-down-49-since-1993-peak-public-unaware/) 
[The number of mass shootings has stayed statistically the same.](https://www.politico.com/magazine/story/2017/10/04/mass-shootings-more-deadly-frequent-research-215678)
1.3.8. Con: -> See 1.3.7.2.4.6.1.
1.3.9. Pro: Strict gun control is the only mechanism that can put guns in the hands of law abiding citizens while keeping them out of the hands of criminals.
1.3.9.1. Pro: Strict gun control is a strong deterrent for those who wish to obtain guns for ill purposes, and any deterrent is a good one in this case.
1.3.9.2. Con: It is already illegal to use guns in crimes, what laws would make a criminal or someone who intends to commit their first criminal act stop and change their mind.  Murder, kidnapping, assault, etc. are all illegal already, yet they happen in spite of the laws.
1.3.9.2.1. Con: This arguments fails to distinguish between laws that prevent criminals from being able to commit a crime \(ie, gun control laws seek to keep the means from an individual that would use them from harm\) vs laws that punish a crime \(ie, murderers go to jail\).
1.3.9.2.2. Pro: How is it a problem if longer prison sentences for violent crimes prevent criminal from being on the street to commit additional crimes.  Criminals will always find ways to commit crimes, but if they realize that the punishment is severe enough like Project Exile, then they may think twice or commit a less severe crime or not use a firearm.[Project Exile](https://www.crimesolutions.gov/ProgramDetails.aspx?ID=413)
1.3.10. Pro: The ultimate goal must be safety.  Similar to how we take the time and inconvenience to secure our homes.  We shouldn’t have to, but it is sensible and unfortunately necessary.  The same principle applies \(albeit on a very different scale\) to it being sensible and necessary to sacrifice the freedom of gun ownership.
1.3.10.1. Con: Safety is one goal, but to some, freedom is the more ultimate goal.  People have the right to choose their own ultimate goal.
1.3.10.1.1. Pro: We could almost certainly eliminate nearly all crime if we implemented oppressive universal surveillance, but we consider this to be an illegitimate invasion of privacy. This means that there is a balance between freedom and safety that society is trying to find.
1.3.10.1.1.1. Con: We only have issues with surveillance because humans are involved, and humans have a propensity for bias and abuse of power.
1.3.10.1.1.1.1. Con: Humans would necessarily be involved in any form of surveillance related to gun control or any other government function, so any system of surveillance or permitting would inherently be as flawed as the human beings in charge of it.
1.3.10.1.1.1.1.1. Pro: Any surveillance program that is given too much power is therefore a likely vector of institutional tyranny that could make people less safe from the very people and systems the public has put in place to keep them safe. As the saying goes, "Who shall watch the watchers? Who shall police the police?"
1.3.10.1.1.1.2. Pro: The fact that humans are flawed and corruptible is the very reason that the right to gun ownership was put in place as a failsafe against tyrannical systems and government intrusion into civilian life without just cause or due process.
1.3.10.1.2. Con: Some form of legal regulation is necessary in a civilized society to allow people the de facto ability to exercise their de jure rights.
1.3.10.1.2.1. Pro: People need to be able to exercise their freedoms in order to be truly free. A world without laws is likely to be too dangerous for people to feel safe fully exercising their legal freedoms.
1.3.10.1.2.2. Con: Total freedom is the absence of all restrictions.
1.3.10.1.2.2.1. Con: Regulations and rights are a compromise between lawlessness and oppression which allows the most freedom and the most safety.
1.3.10.1.2.3. Pro: The absence of all restrictions is not total freedom, it is anarchy.  Basically the strongest, most heavily armed or most powerful gang gets what they want but everyone else is a victim.
1.3.10.2. Con: Sacrificing self-defense in the name of public safety is a fundamentally self-contradicting idea.
1.3.10.3. Con: This claim presupposes that the government is capable of defending all of its citizens.  The reason for such a lack of safety is most directly related to the lack of the government to enforce the rules currently on the books.[Failure of Government to Enforce Current Safety and Gun Control Laws](https://www.kialo.com/argument/3346.2011)
1.3.11. Pro: Gun control would help fight organised crime.
1.3.11.1. Con: Suspension of constitutional rights including the 4th, 6th and 8th amendments would also do this. That doesn't mean they're good ideas.
1.3.11.1.1. Con: There's a large difference between prohibitions on state violence \(8th\), or guarantees of a fair trial \(4th and 6th\) and prohibitions on access to a particular type of item.
1.3.11.2. Con: Prohibitions generally don't harm organized crime. In fact, organized crime generally profits from them.
1.3.11.3. Pro: A great percentage of illegal gun trade crosses the US-Mexican border, making the Mexican narco-trade uncontrollable and dangerous. New gun controls have led to the [arrest](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/wonk/wp/2016/01/14/why-mexicos-drug-cartels-love-americas-gun-laws/?utm_term=.611052cc7a52) of drug cartel criminals.
1.3.11.3.1. Con: Eric Holder and President Obama intentionally sent guns across the border to Mexico in their 'Fast and Furious' operation [foxnews.com](http://www.foxnews.com/politics/2017/06/07/fast-and-furious-report-slams-holder-doj-for-deception-in-gun-running-scandal.html).  When the government is willing to break the law in this manner, they can not be trusted to be concerned about the best interest of their citizens whether it is safety or other issues, nor can they be trusted to disarm law abiding citizens.
1.3.11.3.2. Con: According to igarape.org.br only 2.2% of all US gun sales go to Mexico.  2.2% of anything is likely to slip through the crack regardless of how vigilant we are.
1.3.11.4. Pro: Many of the guns that end up in terrorist and criminal hands [are legally purchased in the US](https://www.netflix.com/title/80088564), and eventually make their way to [South American](https://www.npr.org/sections/thetwo-way/2016/01/12/462781469/in-mexico-tens-of-thousands-of-illegal-guns-come-from-the-u-s) gangs. Strict control will increase the costs on illegal organizations, thus weakening them.
1.3.11.4.1. Con: Last time I checked, Netflix shows are not news or scientifically documented studies.
1.3.11.4.2. Con: "Gun control would raise the price of legal weapons, making it harder for people who do qualify for a firearm to obtain one
1.3.11.5. Pro: The reason illegal gun trade can happen so easily is because states have vastly different gun laws. [Smugglers in Illinois](https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2015/11/12/us/gun-traffickers-smuggling-state-gun-laws.html) just drive to Indiana, make large purchases and then drive back. Universal gun regulation would easily prevent this.
1.3.11.5.1. Con: This is covered under federal and state laws and is not legal.  [freebeacon.com](http://freebeacon.com/issues/gun-group-calls-for-investigation-into-documentary/) "It would appear that a producer of the Katie Couric documentary ‘Under the Gun’ committed at least four federal felonies, one for each firearm he appears to have illegally purchased since the individual was not a resident of Arizona where he purchased the firearms. He may have also violated state criminal statutes," the group said in a Friday statement.
1.3.11.5.1.1. Con: The problem is not that they committed the felonies, it was that they were *allowed* to commit the felonies, implying that even our current laws are not enforced.
1.3.11.6. Con: Stricter gun controls create a market for off the record fire arms. That demand is almost always filled by cartels and other forms of organized crime.
1.3.11.6.1. Pro: See the lessons of prohibition of alcohol - [object.cato.org](https://object.cato.org/sites/cato.org/files/pubs/pdf/pa157.pdf) It caused an increase in crime by definition, and corruption as organized crime filled the needs of the market.
1.3.11.6.1.1. Con: This claim appears to imply that 'more' organized crime would be worse than the sum benefits provided by stricter gun control - which is either unsupported or subjective.
1.3.11.6.1.2. Con: The premise of your argument rests on the fact that all alcohol was completely banned during prohibition and therefore organized crime rings were the only suppliers. Unlike here, where guns will still be widely for sale legally, diminishing the possibility of organized crime taking any portion of that market.
1.3.11.6.1.3. Pro: Many gun owners believe that the end goal is to ban all firearms, regardless of claimed intent.  This is due to multiple reasons including the targets of stricter controls change over time, and as certain weapons become unavailable, either newer types would be developed or other existing weapons would be used instead, and then bans and restrictions would be sought for these weapons.
1.3.11.6.1.4. Pro: Since it was a black market the operators could not depend on police for protection, nor could they resolve disputes in the courts. Nor could they insure their product. Violence was inevitable.
1.3.12. Pro: Promoting a safe society and caring for the lives of others is central to American values.
1.3.12.1. Con: The founders believed that allowing people to keep and bear arms did promote a safe society, and cared for the lives of others by providing all citizens a means for their own defense. American values rejected entirely the idea that infringing on individual rights promoted a safe society, or promoted the idea that "caring for the lives of others" was accomplished by leaving others defenseless against attack by either criminals or the state itself.
1.3.12.1.1. Con: The Framers of the Constitution specifically discouraged taking up arms against the State in Article 1, Section 8.  Suppressing insurrection is referred to multiple times in the Constitution.
1.3.12.1.2. Con: The individual right to arms not subject to militia service is a recent notion stemming from the 2008 Supreme Court decision in Heller.
1.3.13. Pro: Weapons technology and lethality has advanced dramatically since the Second Amendment, and will continue to advance into the future. Just as we've banned private citizens from owning attack helicopters and grenades, we will face increasingly unacceptable mass-casualty events unless we restrict weapons designed to kill lots of people quickly.
1.3.13.1. Con: The problem with this idea is that semi-automatic firearms have been around for a very long time, as early as 1903. Every single rifle used in a mass shooting has been semi-automatic. Suggesting that there are substantial technical differences between the guns of 1950 and the guns of today is slightly to seriously inaccurate. The first production semi-auto was the Winchester model 1903. [en.wikipedia.org](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winchester_Model_1903). There were earlier versions by other manufacturers but they were not widely available.
1.3.13.1.1. Con: This does not undermine the claim, which is that weapons have advanced since the 2nd Amendment was adopted, which was 1791, not 1903. The claim didn't even suggest that there are substantial differences between guns of 1950 and today, it is claiming that there are differences between guns of 1791 and today. A completely different argument.
1.3.13.2. Con: -> See 1.3.11.6.1.
1.3.13.3. Pro: The original language of the 2nd Amendment is quite vague, and can be interpreted to have many different meanings. The vague wording combined with technological and social changes since its writing should allow for very broad interpretation of gun control. That is to say that it is still within the Constitution to institute very broad and very strict weapons controls and/or bans without infringing upon the Constitution.
1.3.13.3.1. Con: The text of the 2nd Amendment isn't vague at all.  The only part that dictates a restriction quite clearly and simply states that the right of the people to both keep and bear arms shall not be infringed.
1.3.13.3.1.1. Con: Infringement does not include regulation in its definition.
1.3.13.3.2. Con: Technological and social changes have no bearing on the law.  Similar to how protection of free speech automatically applies to the internet, and protection against cruel and unusual punishment means that modern torture methods are still prohibited by the 8th.
1.3.13.3.2.1. Pro: The SCotUS has held that “the Second Amendment extends, prima facie, to all instruments that constitute bearable arms, even those that were not in existence at the time of the founding,” District of Columbia v. Heller, 554 U. S. 570, 582 \(2008\)
1.3.13.3.3. Con: "A well regulated Militia, being necessary to the security of a free State, the right of the people to keep and bear Arms, shall not be infringed." ...is not vague.
1.3.13.3.3.1. Pro: [10 U.S. Code § 246](https://www.law.cornell.edu/uscode/text/10/246) explains "The militia of the United States consists of all able-bodied males at least 17 years of age and, except as provided in section 313 of title 32, under 45 years of age who are, or who have made a declaration of intention to become, citizens of the United States and of female citizens of the United States who are members of the National Guard."
1.3.13.3.3.1.1. Con: This definition would bar gun ownership from anyone younger than 17 and older than 45, people not eligible physically for military service, and women.
1.3.13.4. Con: The founding fathers intended that the people have the means to overthrow the military of their own government should that government become corrupt. Infantry weaponry of the day is the bare minimum to accomplish such a goal, if necessary. Although technology has changed, the need for revolution and the root of human corruption do not change with time. For the people to adequately defend against a tyrannical military, they must have equivalent firepower at their disposal.

1.3.13.4.2. Con: The 2nd amendment was written to allow state militias to maintain arms and was included so that states who, under British rule, had full access to fire arms were more likely to sign on to the new federal government. It wasn't until two rulings by the SCotUS  as late as 2010 that cemented full rights to private citizens. Full history can be found here. [en.wikipedia.org](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution)
1.3.13.4.3. Con: This is utter nonsense. The Constitution giving the populace the right to vote prevents this more effectively.
1.3.13.4.4. Con: This argument would mean people should have access to Artillery, Tanks, Warships, and Combat Aircraft, if not nuclear weapons, most of which are prohibited by arms control and legislation, not to mention being prohibitively expensive for private citizens.
1.3.13.5. Pro: Restricting access to semi-auto, external box magazine fed firearms will lower the number of casualties in mass shooting, and do not serve a unique purpose that cannot be fulfilled by either:
A\) a pump/lever/bolt action, external box magazine fed firearm, or;
B\) a semi-auto, fixed size internal magazine fed firearm.
1.3.13.5.1. Con: The fact that police choose to use magazine fed semi-auto weapons for their jobs, which most certainly do not entail mass murder, indicates very strongly that standard semi-auto weapons and magazines are more useful in lawful defensive situations, and therefore restricting them would negatively impact legal defensive gun use, resulting in far more casualties than those from mass shootings.
1.3.13.6. Con: The RATIFIED language of the 2nd Amendment may seem vague, but if you study the evolution of the amendment from its origins in anti-federalists papers through ratification you will clearly see its intent was that all people be allowed to own all arms. "The militia" means "the body of the people" and arms at the time included cannons. [A Century of Lawmaking for a New Nation: US Congressional Documents and Debates, 1774-1875, Journal of the Seante of the United States of America, Volume 1, p. 63](http://rs6.loc.gov/cgi-bin/ampage?collId=llsj&fileName=001/llsj001.db&recNum=60&itemLink=r%3Fammem%2Fhlaw%3A%40field%28DOCID%2B%40lit%28sj001133%29%29%230010075&linkText=1)
1.3.13.6.1. Con: If militia meant "the body of the people" and if we want to hold onto the meanings of the time, then we need a well-regulated body of people according to Section 8 in the Constitution and the Second Amendment. That is, compulsory training and discipline.
1.3.13.7. Con: The 2nd Amendment operates independent of its time period. Making this argument is like saying that protections of the 1st amendment don’t apply today because all we had at the time were public speaking forums and newspapers. Therefore 1st amendment protections don’t apply to today’s telecommunications \(phone, tv, internet, radio, etc.\). This is obviously not the case.
1.3.13.8. Pro: The second amendment was written in 1792. At that time, most guns were very inaccurate and could only fire one bullet at a time and not very quickly at that - maybe 3 shots in a minute. Today, an AR-15 can fire 100 rounds per minute, and the laws need to adjust to the [technological change](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=EM3vlPPNFVM).
1.3.14. Pro: [Different studies demonstrate](https://www.americanprogress.org/issues/guns-crime/reports/2016/10/11/145830/america-under-fire/) that there is a strong and significant link between weak gun laws and high rates of gun violence.  The 10 states with the weakest gun laws collectively have an aggregate level of gun violence that is 3.2 times higher than the 10 states with the strongest gun laws.
1.3.14.1. Con: And yet New Hampshire, the state with the lowest murder rate in the country, has loose gun control laws, much like [8 out of the 10](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Murder_in_the_United_States_by_state) states with the lowest murder rates.  If you're going by correlation, that indicates that while loose gun control laws might result in higher percentages of crimes committed with guns, the overall murder/violent crime rates go down.  Given that the goal is to save lives, and fewer people die with loose gun control, it is clearly the better system.
1.3.14.1.1. Con: New Hampshire [has the 5th lowest Gun Ownership percent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gun_violence_in_the_United_States_by_state), which may help cause of the low murder rates.
1.3.14.2. Con: These studies, and others like them, only demonstrate a correlation or relationship. They do not establish any kind of causality. The weak gun laws \(A\) and higher levels of gun violence \(B\) could both be caused by other factors.  So, if A and B are both caused by factors D, E, & F then changing A will not necessarily change B.
1.3.14.3. Con: The cited study in the claim above factors "suicide by gun" into "gun violence". This skews the numbers immensely \(~66%\), and is misleading. Suicide should not be considered "gun violence", because the "aggressor" in a suicide does not infringe anyone else's rights.
1.3.14.4. Con: [54% of US counties in 2014 had zero murders, 2% of counties have 51% of the murders](https://crimeresearch.org/2017/04/number-murders-county-54-us-counties-2014-zero-murders-69-1-murder/). Many of the highest-homicide rate areas also have the most strict gun regulations: Chicago, Baltimore, Washington D.C., Los Angeles, NYC, etc. Of course correlation does not equal causation, but this proves that more regulation does not prevent crime.

1.3.17. Pro: The country would be safer if we had fewer things that were specifically designed to kill.
1.3.17.1. Pro: When cars were first invented people were dying in much higher rates than today.[We came together, realized there was a problem and worked together to solve it.](http://www.detroitnews.com/story/news/local/michigan-history/2015/04/26/auto-traffic-history-detroit/26312107/) Now cars are much safer than what they used to be, and still are a massive part of our society. We can do the same with guns. There are solutions that we can take to make guns safer that law abiding gun owners shouldn't have a problem adjusting to.
1.3.17.1.1. Con: Guns are not cars but if they were then you could purchase, possess and use them without license, insurance, registration, ID, background check and etc. While not all items listed are required for a car, those requirements that do apply are for the use of them on public roads, not private ownership.
1.3.17.1.1.1. Pro: The regulations on cars that have made us safer are structural regulations like seatbelts, firewalls and airbags. Firearms have similar safety requirements as well.
1.3.17.1.2. Pro: Cars and weapons are different. Guns were invented primarily as a tool for killing things, and cars were made to transport people. Misuse of cars can result in death, but a person must be willing to take a life if they decide to fire a gun at a person.
1.3.17.1.2.1. Con: There are plenty of things you can do with guns, such as hunting, sport shooting, and collecting, that can be part of a good life.
1.3.17.1.2.2. Con: That's false as well. There are plenty of times a gun can be used for good without actually having to shoot it and/or kill someone. For example: A large criminal brandishes a knife and states his intention to murder a civilian nearby. A civilian points a gun at them and tells them to stop and lie on the ground. In most cases, not wanting to be shot causes the criminal to stop that activity. Life is not lost, and had an unarmed person tried to stop the criminal, that may not have been the case.
1.3.17.1.3. Con: That's true, and it's also why guns are also much safer than they used to be.  Just as safety belts, airbags, and seat belts were added to cars, features like trigger safeties, suppressors, and barrel shrouds make guns much safer to use than before, which is why accidental deaths from guns are at about 500 per year in a population of 100 million legal gun owners, a rate far, FAR lower than accidental deaths from cars.
1.3.17.1.4. Pro: Yes, we need to stop trying to ban safety features like barrel shrouds \(prevent burns\), suppressors \(prevent hearing damage\), and telescoping stocks \(allow shooters of different heights to more securely shoulder a rifle, lowering the possibility of an accident\).  Law abiding gun-control advocates should have no problem adjusting to these things.

1.3.17.4.1. Con: Since the supply of existing firearms is incredibly vast, no such guarantees of additional safety could be made just by additional regulation.
1.3.17.4.2. Con: This assumes that the rate of offence will also be reduced by gun control. However many offenders do not need guns to continue offending.
1.3.17.4.2.1. Pro: Many people feel safer with guns and training to protect themselves. Relying on the government for safety is truly a gamble and in the end an illusion. Responsible gun owners understand this; they train themselves and in the end that is the highest percentage chance of being safe. The government cannot make you any safer: it is just an illusion.

1.3.22. 1.3.22.1. Con: Criminals inherently do not follow Society’s laws. Criminals who have access to firearms do so by breaking Society’s laws, in this case, by acquiring said firearms [illegally, by stealth or violence.](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/wonk/wp/2016/07/27/new-evidence-confirms-what-gun-rights-advocates-have-been-saying-for-a-long-time-about-crime/) Therefore stricter firearm ownership will not effectively [remove firearms from criminal possession.](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5385318/)

1.3.22.1.3. Pro: “Past research has demonstrated that a small fraction of gun dealers are responsible for the majority of guns used in crimes in the United States. A 2000 report from the Bureau of Alcohol, Tobacco and Firearms found that in 1998, more than 85 percent of gun dealers had no guns used in crimes trace back to them. By contrast, 1 percent of dealers accounted for nearly 6 in 10 crime gun traces that year.”[washingtonpost.com](https://www.washingtonpost.com/news/wonk/wp/2016/07/27/new-evidence-confirms-what-gun-rights-advocates-have-been-saying-for-a-long-time-about-crime/)

Empiricism is critical to addressing the efficacy of such laws.

1.4.3.4.3.2.2.1.1. Con: OK, sure, but n=44, which is hardly exhaustive. We know that the incidence of toddler perpetrated gun homicide is quite low--I would go as far as to say zero. Including people who are automatically tried as adults in blurbs and charts referring to "children" is deceptive.

1.4.3.4.3.6. Con: There are regulations about the age of a purchaser or owner, but gun safety, hunting and firearms training very often begins at a young age. Gun ranges were regular features of public schools in the mid 20th century. If there's a need to change the way kids approach firearms, perhaps we should not have demonized them and created a mystique around something that was commonplace in homes, communities and even schools.
1.4.3.4.3.6.1. Pro: In environments where guns are encountered by children, by parents, relatives, or friends who own them and introduce them to the home, early education on the proper handling, storage, and purpose of firearms is important for their well-being and safety.
1.4.3.4.3.6.1.1. Pro: I'm all for proper storage, but you can't enforce it in homes and people throw guns away in order to not have them after committing crimes.  There are lots of reasons why kids may encounter unlocked guns that they should be prepared for. Every one of my kids has been able quote the rules since well before they could work the action: 

1. Stop
2. Don't Touch
3. Leave the Area
4. Tell an Adult

This should be taught from a very early age by parents and, yes, in classrooms.
1.4.3.4.3.6.1.2. Con: This helps prevent accidental death, but does little to nothing to prevent adolescent suicide/homicide attempts.

Nobody I know keeps their car keys in a safe and nearly every parent has a car we could also claim that children have access to otherwise legally owned cars.  Car ownership is not a right and neither is alcohol.
1.4.3.4.4. Con: Our nation decided that the age of majority is 18 because at that age most people have become aware of the difference between right and wrong and have the mental capacity to understand their rights and responsibilities as citizens.

This wouldn't mean any restrictions on legal gun owners, other than their responsibility to make sure their firearms, whatever kind, and however many, are stored appropriately under lock and key.
1.4.3.4.5.1. Con: This would be difficult to implement as people can lie, thefts can occur, children can get their hands on the guns anyway, etc. all of which would make proving negligence in court really difficult.
1.4.3.4.5.2. Pro: When an owner is negligent enough that their weapon is stolen and used for a crime, they should be held liable.
1.4.3.4.5.2.1. Con: Owners should not be held liable if they informed the police of the theft in a timely manner. You cannot hold the victim of a crime liable for the actions of the person who committed the crime.
1.4.3.4.5.2.1.1. Con: There should also be a reasonable level of care when it comes to safeguarding the weapon. This is an absurd example but still technically legal in most states: a gun owner could lay all of their firearms and ammunition out on their front porch with a big sign saying "GUNS!" and then go on vacation. Surely even if they came home a week later and reported all of their guns stolen they should still be liable for criminal negligence with a firearm.
1.4.3.4.5.2.2. Pro: -> See 1.3.2.2.1.1.
1.4.3.4.5.2.3. Con: Banks have great security and they still get robbed.  You wish to hold private citizens to a higher standard than banks with their vaults and security guards / police officers.
1.4.3.4.5.2.3.1. Con: Banks are responsible to give a reasonable level of care, or at least to be candid about their security measures and insurance in the event of theft. This is enforced by policy and the demands of their customers. The public would prefer not to be shot by a stolen \(or any\) firearm, but they cannot enforce this demand without policy.
1.4.3.4.5.2.3.1.1. Con: How does this invalidate my statement.  Unless the government is going to guarantee that citizens have inpenetrable houses there is no way to stop burglaries, regardless of what is stolen.
1.4.3.4.5.2.3.1.1.1. Con: Negligence is the crime, not penetrable defenses. Banks, police, and citizens who choose to be negligent with property, i.e. not provide a reasonable amount of care or security, should be held liable for the negligence, especially when it leads to greater crimes due to failure to report in a timely manner.
1.4.3.4.5.2.3.1.1.1.1. Con: The claim is that anyone who owns guns that get stolen should be held liable for their future misuse because they are negligent. This is equivalent to saying that if your car is stolen and used in the commission of other crimes that you should be liable.
1.4.3.4.5.2.3.2. Con: Appropriate storage of a firearm can be as simple as placing it in a locked cabinet, in a locked room. Appropriate care can be as simple as verifying it is safe and properly stored at reasonable intervals, which would vary by legislation and circumstance.
1.4.3.4.5.3. Pro: There's already a federal law requiring the provision of a lock for all firearms with all sales other than private sales - this could be strengthened.

1.4.3.4.5.4.1. Con: With a proper security system, dog, and strong locking doors, you will have ample warning before the assailant is inside. Time to call the police, secure your family, and retrieve your weapon from the quick release handprint safe that you use as your nightstand.

My dogs didn't start barking until he got to the steps and moments before he shot the door, I barely had the time to grab the shot gun \(I keep it slinged off my headboard\) and put one in the chamber before he was in my house, If my only gun was in a safe, or locked in a nightstand, I would have been in trouble. As for a biometric safe, I don't trust them due to difficulty reading sweaty hands.

South Korea has VERY strict gun control, yet has a higher rate of suicides at 28.3 per 100,000 while the US has 14.3 per 100,000. This proves that guns do not increase suicide and that suicides should not be included in the calculations.

1.4.8.4.1. Con: This argument assumes that it will not or might not be successful. An argument against doing something because it "might" not work is very different than one against something because it "will" not work.
1.4.8.4.2. Con: This advocates doing nothing because it "might" not work. Based on that rationale, nothing should ever be done and the status quo never altered, because it "might not work". This is a very negative attitude and position to take and means the situation can never improve.
1.4.8.5. Pro: There is no reason the USA could not introduce the stricter gun controls proposed, as plenty of other countries have. The idea however is resisted due to an entrenched gun culture as well as highly lucrative pro-gun group financial lobbying and propaganda.
1.4.8.5.1. Con: The pro-gun lobby you speak of is the NRA and over half their funding comes from [membership dues](http://www.amarkfoundation.org/nra-who-funds-the-nra-11-13-15.pdf). That means that it is individuals that are defending their own rights, not some large corporate scheme. Furthermore, they spend less on lobbying than they spend on simply [keeping their members informed on which politician is pro-gun or anti-gun](https://www.nytimes.com/2018/02/24/us/politics/nra-gun-control-florida.html). That affects their voting and can easily keep anti-gun politicians from being elected.
1.4.8.5.1.1. Con: That they can and do [influence politics](https://www.politifact.com/truth-o-meter/article/2017/oct/11/counting-up-how-much-nra-spends/) and politicians with [lobbying and activism](https://www.opensecrets.org/orgs/summary.php?id=D000000082&cycle=2016) is not refuted by the above claim, but rather supported.
1.4.8.5.1.1.1. Con: The NRA does not heavily influence politics by lobbying. [For all of 2017, The NRA spent a total of $5 million on various lobbying.](https://www.opensecrets.org/orgs/summary.php?id=D000000082&cycle=2018) [That's less than Verizon, Amazon and Facebook have each spent so far in 2018](https://www.opensecrets.org/lobby/top.php?showYear=2018&indexType=s). The NRAs primary power comes from making information available to members so that they can vote for the candidates they feel best represents their interests.
1.4.8.5.1.1.1.1. Con: Even if companies like Verizon and Facebook lobby more, that does not make the NRA's lobbying not meaningful- it's more likely that Facebook and Verizon also have outsize power in Washington.
1.4.8.5.1.1.1.2. Con: The way the NRA presents power to members affects their members voting decisions, so the NRA can use this to select which candidates they want to portray in a positive light.
1.4.8.6. Con: You are conflating gun control with a reduction in the number of guns available. The two are not the same. Gun control makes legally obtaining a new gun harder, but it does nothing to eliminate the 393 million guns already in circulation. Additionally, if a gun law were implemented requiring surrendering certain firearms or even just registering them, there would be massive civil disobedience like what happened with [New York's SAFE Act](https://hudsonvalleyone.com/2016/07/07/massive-noncompliance-with-safe-act/).

We seem comfortable arguing for federal authority on some and not on others.  We should research cause/affect throughout the states to determine what root causes may be and what solutions work best.

1.4.12.1. Pro: Most Americans prefer to keep their property or at least have some control over disposing of it. Forcing people to hand over property whether it is their home, their car, their guns, or other property deprives them of the right to set their own price and have any choice about selling it. I think after some thought most intelligent people would want to avoid the potential criminal record and sell back the guns.

1.4.14. Pro: Gun control can never eliminate "cheating" the law, and in fact tend to motivate more lethal alternatives. For instance, full-auto guns are banned by the ATF, but bump stocks mimic full-auto fire on a technically semi-automatic firearm. Allegedly, bump stocks were "intended to assist persons whose hands have limited mobility to ‘bump-fire’ an AR-15 type rifle.” but end up being used by able persons to mimic full-auto fire in a semi-automatic weapon.   [Bump Stocks Allegedly Made for The Disabled](https://mic.com/articles/184982/bump-stocks-were-supposedly-made-for-disabled-people-thats-not-how-theyre-actually-being-used#.E9kV2Mdr9)
1.4.14.1. Con: The technology may be becoming more advanced, but further regulation of bump stocks for example, is absolutely apart of the larger gun control effort. The way forward is to update our legislation as the technology advances.
1.4.15. Pro: Recent events have proven that the current regulatory landscape is not properly enforced. Why would anyone support more regs before those enforcement deficiencies are corrected?
1.4.15.1. Con: We use policy to communicate priorities. The relatively lax regulations on guns communicates that the government does not take gun regulation seriously. A world where the government implements strong regulations is likely to be one where the people enforcing the regulations take them more seriously as well.
1.4.15.2. Pro: If we assume a consistent level of competence for enforcing gun laws, any new regulation will fail.
1.4.15.3. Con: Regulatory measures and enforcement measures are not mutually exclusive. Deficiencies are a reality of any type of enforcement. The presence of deficiencies does not restrict legislation from being improved. Furthermore, the improved regulations may promote better conditions for effective enforcement.
1.4.15.3.1. Pro: The presence of regulations would act as a motivating power to avoid unnecessary gun use among law-abiding citizens reducing the overall need for enforcement.
1.4.15.3.2. Pro: Organised system of conditions that should be met for gun use would allow the law enforcement to have additional data about abusers to make informed decisions.
1.4.15.3.3. Pro: Necessity of following specific procedures and information disclosure will prevent individuals with malicious intent from buying guns through official channels. That would also make it easier for enforcement to identify illegal use.
1.4.15.4. Con: Current regulations fail because there are influential organizations making sure that they are designed in a way that makes them practically impossible to enforce.
1.4.15.4.1. Pro: According to [this article](https://thehill.com/blogs/congress-blog/judicial/281559--give-law-enforcement-the-power-to-enforce-current-gun-laws), the NRA actually wrote their own ammendments which heavily restrict background checks, inventory checks, and access to gun crime data by state and local law enforcement, all of which makes it practically impossible for the ATF to enforce existing laws.

1.4.32.1. Con: The plastics used in 3D printing are too brittle to make a terribly functional gun, and a metal-based 3D printer is likely to be so expensive as to not be a [meaningful alternative](https://3dprint.com/139537/3d-printed-guns/).
1.4.32.2. Con: Laws very rarely or never perfectly solve the problems they mean to address, but that doesn't mean their implementation is futile. For example, methamphetamine is still manufactured despite the [drug laws](https://www.zdnet.com/article/buy-too-much-sudafed-and-you-may-get-a-visit-from-a-cop/) that make it harder to acquire the necessary chemicals.
1.4.33. Pro: The suggested actions would be impossible, given how few guns in the United States are registered to anyone. Any government buy-back program would function entirely on the honor system, and there is no reason to believe criminals using guns for the purpose of committing crimes would have any interest in turning in their guns that no one would have any way of knowing they own to begin with.
1.4.34. Pro: Efforts to control the number of small arms in the US by imposing a uniform criteria for their ownership and usage ,as suggested, would be ineffective here. The United States is still in a maturing stage as a society, yet composed of various ethnic and cultural tribes practicing a form of feudalistic federalism. The tribes recognize foremost their own control and belittle centralized authority. The first impulse in tribal America is to try to skirt the law to maintain feudalistic integrity.
1.4.35. Pro: -> See 1.3.7.2.2.1.4.
1.4.36. Pro: The suggested policies will be enforced by an entity which is itself responsible for multiple mass killings of unarmed citizens \(e.g. [Kent State Massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kent_State_shootings), [Wounded Knee Massacre](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wounded_Knee_Massacre), [Waco Seige](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Waco_siege), etc\). Additionally, the number of [paramilitary home raids](https://object.cato.org/sites/cato.org/files/pubs/pdf/balko_whitepaper_2006.pdf) has been increasing in recent years, many of which take place at the [wrong address](https://the7thpwr.wordpress.com/accidental-police-shootings/).

1.7. Con: People like playing with guns \(eg FPSRussia or similar\) and they should not have to be limited to the particular uses of the gun as per the proposed restrictions.
1.7.1. Pro: Governments generally seek to maximise the happiness of their citizens by allowing them to do things they enjoy.
1.7.1.1. Con: Sometimes, these things people enjoy might be dangerous to not only themselves, but also people around them. The potential safety of many is more important than the potential joy of the few.
1.7.1.1.1. Con: That depends on the society in which you want to live. I think many people would prefer some balance between risk and safety.
1.7.1.1.2. Con: We allow NASCAR, dirt track and Indy races because the participants and spectators enjoy them.  Nobody can deny that racing \(whether illegal or legal\) is dangerous.
1.7.1.2. Con: That which governments generally do does not determine which policies are best practice.
1.7.2. Con: It is possible to strike a balance between allowing people to access guns for recreational use, and restricting the sale of guns to potentially dangerous people.
1.7.3. Con: This law would not preclude people from playing with guns. There could still be legal gun shows and shooting ranges where anyone could get in and play with as many guns as they wanted.
1.7.3.1. Con: It would, however, preclude them from using the guns to defend themselves as self-defense is not one of the uses listed. That's a showstopper.
1.7.3.2. Con: "Sport Shooting" is one of the use-cases listed, which includes most safe uses of guns for fun.
1.7.4. Con: The purpose of government is to keep people safe, not to ensure that they get to do the things they like doing. For example, people really like camping in remote areas but the government regulates certain campsites to make sure people do not disrupt wildlife or get mauled by bears.
1.7.4.1. Con: According to the [Declaration of Independence](http://www.ushistory.org/declaration/document/), the purpose of government is to secure the rights of a nation's people; however should a government overstep its bounds in this regard, it is the right of the people to alter or abolish it.
1.7.4.2. Con: Keeping people safe can go too far, and become a form of paternalistic tyranny that oppresses its people "for their own good."
1.7.4.2.1. Con: The proposed regulation is not a totalitarian ban on gun ownership. Controlling who was access to certain potentially dangerous activities in society already exists, eg. Driving Licences. You are only able to drive while you can demonstrate that you can do so without risk to public safety.
1.7.5. Con: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.2.
1.7.6. Con: Literal [toys](http://www.independent.co.uk/life-style/food-and-drink/features/why-are-kinder-surprise-eggs-illegal-in-the-usa-10055273.html) are routinely banned in the US for safety reasons.
1.7.6.1. Pro: Lawn Darts were banned from being sold in the U.S. after [three children were killed](https://www.cpsc.gov/content/following-recent-injury-cpsc-reissues-warning-lawn-darts-are-banned-and-should-be-destroyed) by them. People liked playing with them, but they were deemed too dangerous. Meanwhile, [hundreds of people die every year](http://www.aftermath.com/content/accidental-shooting-deaths-statistics) just from accidental shootings.
1.7.6.1.1. Con: That's more of an example of an extreme reaction on the part of people that banned lawn darts than a commentary on gun laws.
1.7.6.2. Con: This includes bans on items considered safe by most of the world including Kinder Eggs. Thus it is not always a public benefit to ban items.
1.7.6.3. Con: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.3.
1.7.6.4. Con: Guns are designed to be useful for adults, not to be safe for children.
1.7.7. Pro: "I like guns" should be considered a valid reason to own/use/collect them in a free society, similar to how "I like fishing" or "I like shoes" is a valid reason for vast collections of fishing gear or shoes. It's no different. The difference is that guns can be used to cause harm, so the focus of any legislation should be whether or not a person is safe to own a gun, not why they want/need to.
1.7.7.1. Con: There are things you cannot collect, because those things are too dangerous. For example, poisonous gases, cocaine samples, virus strains, etc. Guns fall into the same category.
1.7.7.1.1. Con: To own, collect, or use dangerous but inanimate things, a person should only have to prove that they have the ability and intent not to cause harm to others. Their motivations, however strange, should be nobody else's business.
1.7.7.1.1.1. Con: Intent is neither a constant nor measurable. Authorities, if they granted extremely dangerous substances or weapons to a law-abiding citizen who just liked the smell of them \(or some other reason\), would be incapable of mitigating hazards to society if the owner suddenly changed their mind about how the hazardous materials should be used, or failed to keep the materials out of the irresponsible or criminal hands.
1.7.7.1.1.2. Con: Proving a harmless intent would necessarily require stating intent and providing evidence to support that statement. Therefore their motivations are the government's business.
1.7.7.1.1.3. Con: If one collects poison sprayers because they like them \(or use them for other purposes\) but do not use them illegally, they should have no requirement to prove that that should be allowed to purchase and collect them.
1.7.7.1.2. Con: An unloaded gun is not dangerous in and of itself. Poison gases can leak, but bullets and guns are not a danger in and of themselves. Cocaine samples are not a danger, they are just illegal. Virus strains can infect the population if not properly controlled and destroyed when the lab is done with them.
1.7.7.2. Pro: Buying a box of matches could start a whole forest fire and the destruction of many homes. So why do we sell them if they can do so much harm? Because the benefits outweigh the small possibility that you could burn your home down, matches are not illegal. This is the same case with guns. Guns are [used much more often to defend rather than kill](https://www.cnsnews.com/news/article/cdc-study-use-firearms-self-defense-important-crime-deterrent), thus the benefits outweigh the consequences.
1.7.7.2.1. Con: The primary function of a match is not to harm or maim. the threat the matches have posed thus far to public safety is vastly overshadowed by threat guns present.
1.7.7.3. Con: I like "Flamethrowers" doesn't allow you to own functional flamethrowers. Gun Enthusiasts would still be able to own functional guns if they pass the proposed licencing requirements. "Collector" could be an option. Failing enough interest on the gun enthusiast's part to get licenced, one could collect replicas or decommissioned/invalidated guns for a collection.
1.7.8. Con: We can always allow people to "play with guns" in special gun ranges, provided they are properly secured against gun theft, and are held responsible if it does occur.
1.7.9. Con: The ability to play around with a gun isn't worth the danger that a lack of gun control laws provides.
1.7.10. Con: If people would always 'play' with their guns in safe locations where they were at risk but no one else could be harmed, this could be a valid argument. But taking them everywhere and risking other lives is the reason we need better control.
1.7.11. Pro: Trap shooting is great for kids.  It is now the fastest growing sport in the Midwest. Teaches emotional control, calmness, patience, perserverence...
1.8. Pro: There is no inherent natural right to gun ownership.
1.8.1. Con: The right to a firearm is a natural extension of the right to self-defense.
1.8.1.1. Pro: Gun owners need guns to protect their family and loved ones.
1.8.1.1.1. Con: Then high sustained rate of fire should be unnecessary or require stricter regulation. The typical home protection scenario shouldn't mandate an AR-15 with a 30 round clip and a [bump stock](https://youtu.be/Dd9y8hHMUag). A home security system and a pistol or shotgun should be sufficient.
1.8.1.1.1.1. Con: "High capacity" is a relative term, the rate of fire for most guns is "as fast as the trigger can be pulled", and both are irrelevant terms to consider when talking about regulation of self defense, since they are up to the individual person/situation to decide, and vary greatly depending on both.
1.8.1.1.1.2. Pro: Defensive gun use data does not suggest a marginal benefit to home invasion protection provided by high capacity/rate of fire guns. Given that vast majority of defensive gun use incidents don't even involve a shot being fired, having a smaller magazine is unlikely to affect success rates of defensive gun use events.
1.8.1.1.1.3. Con: This argument assumes that citizens only need protection from home invaders.
1.8.1.1.1.4. Con: The "equipment that allows a semi-automatic to achieve the rate of fire of an automatic rifle" \(commonly known as a bump stock\) can be [duplicated using a belt loop](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=wZCO-06qRgY) or a small piece of cloth. Banning bump stocks will not change physics nor the ability to use guns in this way.
1.8.1.1.1.5. Con: A multiple-attacker scenario may necessitate more than a pistol or shotgun.
1.8.1.1.1.5.1. Con: In such a context, your survival chances are relatively low regardless of the weapon you're armed with.
1.8.1.1.1.5.1.1. Con: Tell that to the LA shop owners during the riots.  You literally can.  They lived.
1.8.1.1.1.5.2. Con: -> See 1.3.7.3.3.1.11.
1.8.1.1.1.6. Con: The ability to train oneself in rapid magazine changes makes restrictions in magazine size irrelevant.
1.8.1.1.1.6.1. Con: Since people own guns in order to protect themselves, we should limit guns specifically to what is needed for protection.
1.8.1.1.1.6.1.1. Pro: -> See 1.3.7.3.3.1.11.
1.8.1.1.1.6.1.2. Pro: The right to self defence doesn't necessarily entail the right to own any and all forms of weapon. It's reasonable for a society to agree some limits on the weapons private citizens can own, and indeed existing gun laws already do this.
1.8.1.1.1.6.1.2.1. Con: We have some limits. The right of self defense DOES entail the right to own weapons adequate to meet the threat. Approximately 100 million AR15 rifles have been sold to the public. They're common. They're easy to manufacture with basic shop tools. This means criminals will always have access to them. Adequate defensive capability means the people must have access as well.
1.8.1.1.1.6.1.3. Con: There is no possibility of accurately legislating what is "needed for protection" given any number of different scenarios. Do small women get to use different calibers than large men? Are people in rural areas allowed to use higher caliber rifles since they have to defend larger properties in more open areas? Even if the attempt were made it would not apply to individual men/women/etc. and therefore must be applied to none.
1.8.1.1.1.6.1.4. Con: The only way to accurately determine what was "needed for protection" would be after someone was killed/raped/robbed/etc. and even then one could only determine that their level of protection was insufficient, not the level that would have been needed.
1.8.1.1.1.6.1.5. Pro: -> See 1.3.7.3.3.1.3.1.
1.8.1.1.1.6.1.6. Con: The problem is, who gets to decide what is "needed" and what is not? The point of the right is that this decision is left solely to the individual and not to the opinion of the mob.
1.8.1.1.1.6.1.7. Con: This point is moot since there is no provision for "self-defense" in this proposal.
1.8.1.1.1.6.1.8. Con: What guns would you suggest allowing people to own?  Nearly every gun can be used for self defense as well as sporting purposes.
1.8.1.1.1.6.1.9. Con: -> See 1.2.5.1.1.1.5.

1.8.1.1.1.8. Con: Semiautomatic rifles, despite being used in a fraction of gun crime, allow for a larger sight radius, and can easily come equipped with a flashlight that can be incredibly useful in home invasions.
1.8.1.1.1.9. Con: Even in cases of trained police officers, they only hit their target 30% of the time.  That number [plummets to 13%](http://www.nytimes.com/2008/05/08/nyregion/08nypd.html) when engaged in a gunfight.  The ability to hit the target is augmented/reduced based on the number of rounds in the gun.
1.8.1.1.1.9.1. Pro: All things being equal, that gives a person engaging in gunfire in defense of his home a 98.5% chance of hitting the target with a 30-round magazine, versus a 75.2% chance with a 10-round magazine.
1.8.1.1.2. Con: People can still use tasers, locks, and security systems.
