1.21.2.3.4.1. Con: Yes, but bombs are more likely to replace guns as the weapons of choice if guns become too difficult to obtain, because it is easier to make bombs at your home than firearms.  Nobody can make a gun with diesel and fertilizer or a pressure cooker.

1.21.2.3.4.2. Con: Choosing a different weapon doesn't prevent the murder.
1.21.2.4. Con: While there are many other methods of harming people, none are as lethal and as easily executable, by so many, as a gun.  Gun control isn't meant to prevent all cases of lethal harm but to reduce the frequency in which lethal harm occurs.

Firearms disproportionately advantage the weak, disabled, elderly and female citizens over the strong and those trained and practiced in exercising phyical dominance over others.

I believe criminally minded people feel emboldened knowing there's no CCW holder going to shoot them before the police arrive so they are free to attack as they please.
1.21.3. Pro: Gun control empowers those who wish to own guns with a more secure framework. They can be safe in the knowledge that those who wish to cause harm towards other citizens are restricted from doing so.

This is a self-evident claim, as, obviously it always empowers those that wish for something when given to them.

That doesn't mean that it is beneficiary to anyone else, and being subjective, doesn't even mean that it is actual of benefit to those who want this themselves.

US government protection is not inadequate.[List of countries by military expenditure](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditures)
1.21.12.2.1. Con: The parent claim concerns protection from violent crime and from infringement of individuals' rights by the state, not from attack by a foreign state.
1.21.13. Con: -> See 1.21.9.1.
1.21.14. Con: An avg of 96/365M \(1 in every 3.8M\) people in the United States are victims of deadly gun violence on any given day. I believe the argument to be invalidated mathematically. There is a complaint anecdotally but not statistically. Our government has done a very good job legislating this. Further law modification would only serve to create an unnecessarily inhibitive environment for citizens and create a new class of criminal. Other impacting factors must be improved.[everytownresearch.org](http://everytownresearch.org)
1.21.15. Pro: Living in Canada I almost never worry that the guy walking toward me in the parking lot has a gun and is about to rob me.  Yes, it happens, but it's hard to legally get a gun and illegal guns aren't available unless you know where to look.
1.21.16. Con: The ownership of LEGAL guns shouldn't worry anyone.  Here in Canada legal firearm owners fall far below the national average when it comes to criminality.   I would argue that a legal gun owner is a better neighbor.  Less chance they are going to start a fight or cause trouble and risk losing their hobby!

Also their guns \(here in Canada\) are locked up when stored and when they take them out they are only loaded at the range or in the woods!
1.21.17. Pro: The knowledge that nearly any individual could be carrying a firearm at any moment leads [many people](http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/americas/us-gun-violence-gun-control-ar-15-victims-read-ap-poll-a7152556.html) to be afraid of going outside.
1.21.17.1. Con: Following this logic individuals who do not have guns should feel safer than being around an individual with a gun as more people die from suicide by firearm than homicide annually. 

[www.cdc.gov](https://www.cdc.gov/nchs/fastats/suicide.htm)
1.21.17.1.1. Con: Suicide is a personal choice that the gun owner has control over. People without guns have no control over the actions of people with guns.
1.21.17.1.2. Con: "Being afraid of committing suicide" simply because you have a gun is an absurd concept, and if you are indeed *afraid* of committing suicide, you will probably get rid of the gun.
1.21.17.1.3. Con: It is entirely possible that people have guns exactly because they feel unsafe, and therefore people who do not have guns have a higher baseline level of safety perception.
1.21.17.1.4. Con: People's fears are often not statistically driven. For example, more people are afraid of sharks or flying than driving, despite driving being significantly more dangerous than either of those.
1.21.17.1.4.1. Pro: This is exactly why the desire for more gun control is more about drama than anything else. If you are really afraid of death, eat healthy and exercise. You are far more likely to die of heart disease or [cancer](https://www.google.com/amp/s/www.medicalnewstoday.com/articles/amp/282929) than a bullet wound.
1.21.17.2. Con: The fact that some people suffer Agoraphobia and other psychological issues is not a good reason why people shouldn't be able to defend themselves against crime.
1.21.17.3. Pro: If fewer people went outside, there would be fewer crimes, and therefore fewer deaths.
1.21.17.4. Con: Banning ladders would make people with a fear of heights more comfortable.
1.21.17.4.1. Con: Your fear of ladders does not have the potential to harm others. A Person carrying a concealed firearm does.
1.21.17.4.1.1. Pro: You can choose not to climb a ladder. Others can do nothing about someone carrying a concealed firearm, so the two are not analogous.
1.21.17.4.2. Con: If peoples' fear of heights is more impactful than the harms of banning ladders, then the world is better off with a ladder ban.
1.21.17.5. Pro: If fewer people went outside, there would be fewer victims available for criminals to victimize.
1.21.17.5.1. Con: That's true, but that's effectively imprisoning oneself to protect oneself from crime.
1.21.17.6. Con: Irrational fear is not a reason for legislation that infringes upon the rights of citizens. The knowledge that bacteria exists kept Howard Hughes from going outside as well. That's not a reason to make a law requiring everyone to continually douse themselves in disinfectant every 10 minutes.
1.21.18. Con: It is also possible that knowing "good guys" have guns assuages some of those fears.
1.21.18.1. Pro: -> See 1.2.5.
1.21.18.2. Con: The only 'good guys' are in movies. To the rest of the world, a man with a gun is as reassuring as a man heaving a giant sickle about and just as useful.
1.21.18.3. Con: Many Mass shootings were committed by "good guys" who were "good" up until the moment they were not.  Vegas and Orlando for example.
1.21.19. Pro: The government should take steps not only to make people actually safer, but also to make them feel safer. This is similar to the security theater aspect of the TSA.
1.21.19.1. Pro: The feeling of safety makes a big difference in the daily quality of life of individuals.
1.21.19.1.1. Con: Unless that feeling of safety is based on a false premise.  Using a car with defective airbags or defective seatbelts would not be safe, however the occupants would most likely feel safer if they did not know about the defects.  Using this logic, we should hide all real safety issues so nobody will know about them.
1.21.19.2. Con: -> See 1.3.17.4.2.1.
1.21.19.3. Con: Using the law to control "feelings" would be an impossible task because feelings constantly change and nobody's feelings are the same. Laws should be made based on reason and logic, not feelings.
1.21.19.4. Con: That is true only to the extent that in doing so the government does not infringe upon the rights of its citizens, and even then it is a luxury.
